<span style="font-size: 120%;">↓</span> <a href="/wiki/Future" title="Future">Future</a> <span class="nowrap">  </span></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar" style="background:#f8eaba;padding:0.4em;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Human_history" title="Template:Human history"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Human_history" title="Template talk:Human history"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Human_history&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In many periodizations of <a href="/wiki/Human_history" title="Human history">human history</a>, the <b>late modern period</b> followed the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">early modern period</a>. It began approximately in the mid-18th century and depending on the author either ended with the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_history" title="Contemporary history">contemporary history</a> after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, or includes that period up to the present day. Notable historical milestones included the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a>. It took all of human history up to 1804 for the world's population to reach 1 billion; the next billion came just over a century later, in 1927.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p>

<dd><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#ffd880; color:black;"> </span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#f2d97f; color:black;"> </span> Modern Age <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#cccccc; color:black;"> </span> Other</dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Significant_events">Significant events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Significant events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> and political revolutions in the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">early modern period</a>, the world-views of <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">modernism</a> emerged.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The industrialization of many nations was initiated with the industrialization of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a>. Particular facets of the late modern period include:
</p>
<ul><li>Increasing role of <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a></li>
<li>Spread of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_movements" title="Social movements">social movements</a></li>
<li>Institution of <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism" title="Abolitionism">abolition of slavery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_Imperialism" title="New Imperialism">New Imperialism</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>, and later <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrialization" title="Industrialization">Industrialization</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">Urbanization</a></li>
<li>Increasing role of <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a></li>
<li>Mass <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> and proliferation of <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">mass media</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">Women's rights</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">Socialism</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Demographic_transition" title="Demographic transition">Demographic transition</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Green_Revolution" title="Green Revolution">Green Revolution</a> in agriculture</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Information_Age" title="Information Age">Information Age</a> in the latter 20th and the early 21st century</li></ul>
<p>Other important events in the development of the Late modern period include:
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Opium_Wars" title="Opium Wars">Opium Wars</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unequal_Treaties" title="Unequal Treaties">Unequal Treaties</a> in China (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> mid-19th century</span>)</li>
<li>The failed <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">Revolutions of 1848</a> in Europe</li>
<li>The development of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telegraph" title="Telegraph">telegraph</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> late 18th century</span>) and the adoption of <a href="/wiki/Morse_code" title="Morse code">Morse code</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> mid-19th century</span>)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> (1860–1865) and the <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States" title="Abolitionism in the United States">abolition of slavery in the US</a> (1863–1865)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Meiji_Restoration" title="Meiji Restoration">Meiji Restoration</a> in Japan (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1868</span>)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a> (1870–1871), the <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Germany" title="Unification of Germany">Unification of Germany</a> (1871), and the <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Italy" title="Unification of Italy">Unification of Italy</a> (1871)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a> (1884-1885) and the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/History_of_radio" title="History of radio">development of radio telecommunication</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1894</span>)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> and the American <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine–American War">annexation of the Philippines</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a> (1914–1918) and the fall of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">Austro-Hungarian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> Empires</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement" title="Sykes–Picot Agreement">Sykes–Picot Agreement</a> (1916) between the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_French_Empire" title="Second French Empire">French empires</a> create the modern boundaries of <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a> (1917) and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a> (1917–1922)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence" title="Turkish War of Independence">Turkish War of Independence</a> (1919–1922); the <a href="/wiki/Greek_genocide" title="Greek genocide">Greek</a> (1913–1922), <a href="/wiki/Armenian_genocide" title="Armenian genocide">Armenian</a> (1914–1923), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_genocide" title="Assyrian genocide">Assyrian</a> (1914–1924) genocides</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/March_on_Rome" title="March on Rome">March on Rome</a> and the rise of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fascism_in_Italy" title="Fascism in Italy">Fascism in Italy</a> (1922)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> (1929 – late 1930s) worldwide and the <a href="/wiki/New_Deal" title="New Deal">New Deal</a> in the US</li>
<li>The failed <a href="/wiki/Beer_Hall_Putsch" title="Beer Hall Putsch">Beer Hall Putsch</a> (1923) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hitler%27s_rise_to_power" title="Hitler's rise to power">Hitler's rise to power</a> in Germany (1931–1933)</li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_famine_of_1932%E2%80%931933" title="Soviet famine of 1932–1933">Soviet famine</a> (1932–1933), including the <a href="/wiki/Holodomor" title="Holodomor">Holodomor</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Ukraine" title="Soviet Ukraine">Soviet Ukraine</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kazakh_famine_of_1932%E2%80%931933" title="Kazakh famine of 1932–1933">Kazakh famine</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Kazakhstan" title="Soviet Kazakhstan">Soviet Kazakhstan</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">Japanese invasion of Manchuria</a> (1931) and the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> (1937–1945)</li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> (1939–1945) and <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">The Holocaust</a> in Nazi-occupied Europe (1941–1945)</li>
<li>The Founding of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (1945) as a successor to the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> (1920–1946)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Bengal_famine_of_1943" title="Bengal famine of 1943">Bengal famine</a> (1943) and the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">Partition of India</a> from the British Empire (1947)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a> (beginning 1927) and the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Revolution" title="Chinese Communist Revolution">Chinese Communist Revolution</a> (1945–1949)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> (1947–1991) (including <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Blockade" title="Berlin Blockade">Berlin Blockade</a> (1948–1949), the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> (1950–1953), the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1956" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1956">Hungarian Uprising</a> (1956), the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> (1953–1959) and <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a> (1962), the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> (1955–1975), the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring" title="Prague Spring">Prague Spring</a> in <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> (1968), and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War" title="Soviet–Afghan War">Soviet–Afghan War</a> (1979–1989))</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/De-Stalinization" title="De-Stalinization">De-Stalinization</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> mid-1950s</span>) and the <a href="/wiki/Khrushchev_Thaw" title="Khrushchev Thaw">Khrushchev Thaw</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1950s-early 1960s</span>) in the Soviet Union, and subsequent <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">Sino-Soviet split</a> (1956–1966)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Leap_Forward" title="Great Leap Forward">Great Leap Forward</a> campaign (1958–1962), the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Great_Chinese_Famine" title="Great Chinese Famine">Great Chinese Famine</a> (1959–1961), and the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a> (1966–1976) in China</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights_movement" title="Civil rights movement">1954-1968 civil rights movement</a> in the United States</li>
<li>The first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spaceflights" title="Spaceflights">spaceflights</a>, the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Age" title="Space Age">Space Age</a> (1957–present) and the <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_man_in_space" title="First man in space">first man in space</a> (1961) and the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">first man on the Moon</a> (1969)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1971_Bangladesh_genocide" title="1971 Bangladesh genocide">Bangladesh genocide</a> (1971) and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Liberation_War" title="Bangladesh Liberation War">Bangladesh Liberation War</a> from Pakistan (1971)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a> (1967) and the <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War" title="Yom Kippur War">Yom Kippur War</a> (1973) in Israel, and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">oil embargo</a> against Western countries (1973)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_genocide" title="Cambodian genocide">Cambodian genocide</a> (1975–1979)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution" title="Iranian Revolution">Islamic Revolution in Iran</a> (1979), and the <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War" title="Iran–Iraq War">Iran–Iraq War</a> (1980–1988)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Kuwait" title="Invasion of Kuwait">Iraqi invasion of Kuwait</a> (1990) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf_War" title="Persian Gulf War">Persian Gulf War</a> (1990–1991)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> (1989–1991), and <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">reunification</a> of <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> (1990)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_end_of_the_Late_Modern_period">Possible end of the Late Modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Possible end of the Late Modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are differing approaches to  defining a possible end or conclusion  to the Late Modern period, or indeed whether it might be considered to have concluded at all; if that period is indeed concluded, then there are various options for how to label the subsequent era, i.e. the current contemporary era, as described below.
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Information_Age" title="Information Age">Information Age</a> is a <a href="/wiki/History_by_period" title="History by period">historical period</a> that began in the mid-20th century, characterized by a rapid <a href="/wiki/Epoch" title="Epoch">epochal</a> shift from traditional industry established by the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> to an economy primarily based upon <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Idea_b_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Idea_b-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manuel_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Manuel-5">[5]</a></sup></li>
<li>Some researchers typify the end of the Late Modern period by the concerns for the environment which began in 1950, as this marks the end of modern confidence about humanity's domination of the natural world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Postmodern" title="Postmodern">Postmodern</a> era</i> is the economic or cultural state or condition of society which is said to exist <i>after</i> <a href="/wiki/Modernity" title="Modernity">modernity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[nb 1]</a></sup> Some schools of thought hold that modernity ended in the late 20th century – in the 1980s or early 1990s – and that it was replaced by postmodernity, and still others would extend modernity to cover the developments denoted by postmodernity, while some believe that modernity ended sometime after World War II. The idea of the post-modern condition is sometimes characterized as a culture stripped of its capacity to function in any linear or autonomous state, such as e.g. regressive isolationism, as opposed to the progressive mind state of <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">modernism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup></li></ul>
<dl><dd>Postmodernism is an intellectual stance or mode of discourse<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> defined by an attitude of <a href="/wiki/Philosophical_skepticism" title="Philosophical skepticism">skepticism</a> toward what it describes as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meta-narrative" title="Meta-narrative">grand narratives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ideology" title="Ideology">ideologies</a> of <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">modernism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SEP-2015_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-SEP-2015-11">[10]</a></sup>  It questions or criticizes viewpoints associated with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Enlightenment" title="The Enlightenment">Enlightenment rationality</a> dating back to the 17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-12">[11]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<ul><li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Post-industrial_society" title="Post-industrial society">Post-industrial society</a></i> is the stage of society's development when the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">service sector</a> generates more wealth than the <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Secondary sector of the economy">manufacturing sector</a> of the economy. The term was originated by <a href="/wiki/Alain_Touraine" title="Alain Touraine">Alain Touraine</a> and is closely related to similar sociological theoretical concepts such as <a href="/wiki/Post-Fordism" title="Post-Fordism">post-Fordism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Information_society" title="Information society">information society</a>, <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_economy" title="Knowledge economy">knowledge economy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Post-industrial_economy" title="Post-industrial economy">post-industrial economy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Late_modernity" title="Late modernity">liquid modernity</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Network_society" title="Network society">network society</a>. They all can be used in economics or social science disciplines as a general theoretical backdrop in <a href="/wiki/Research_design" title="Research design">research design</a>. As the term has been used, a few common themes have begun to emerge. Firstly, the economy undergoes a transition from the production of goods to the provision of services; also, producing ideas is the main way to grow the economy. The term is used by various researchers and social scientists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_subdivisions">Possible subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Possible subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Additionally, the Late Modern period can be divided into various smaller periods; there are differing opinions and approaches on which time periods to assert in doing so.
</p>
<ul><li><i>Post-war era.</i> This period refers mainly to social history and domestic economic activity, as it relates to societal progress and the <a href="/wiki/Post%E2%80%93World_War_II_economic_expansion" title="Post–World War II economic expansion">major economic expansion after World War II</a> which occurred in the United States and parts of the Western World.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Postcolonial_Age" title="Postcolonial Age">Postcolonial Era</a>.</i> This relates to the major increase in <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a> which occurred directly as a result of World War II from 1946 onwards, as major European powers formally relinquished political control over almost all of their colonies and overseas possessions, leading to major new countries being formed with full sovereignty.</li>
<li><i>Cold War era.</i> The <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> was a period of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geopolitical" title="Geopolitical">geopolitical</a> tension between the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and their respective allies, the <a href="/wiki/Western_Bloc" title="Western Bloc">Western Bloc</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a>, which began following <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Historians do not fully agree on its starting and ending points, but the period is generally considered to span the 1947 <a href="/wiki/Truman_Doctrine" title="Truman Doctrine">Truman Doctrine</a> (12 March 1947) to the 1991 <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">Dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> (26 December 1991).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> The term <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_war_(general_term)" title="Cold war (general term)">cold war</a></i> is used because there was no large-scale fighting directly between the two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superpowers" title="Superpowers">superpowers</a>, but they each supported major regional conflicts known as <a href="/wiki/Proxy_war" title="Proxy war">proxy wars</a>.</li></ul>
<dl><dd>In 1989, the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_Picnic" title="Pan-European Picnic">Pan-European Picnic</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">peaceful wave of revolutions</a> (with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Revolution" title="Romanian Revolution">Romania</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afghan_Civil_War_(1989-1992)" title="Afghan Civil War (1989-1992)">Afghanistan</a>) overthrew almost all communist governments of the Eastern Bloc. The Communist Party of the Soviet Union itself lost control in the Soviet Union and was banned following an <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt">abortive coup attempt</a> in August 1991. This in turn led to <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">the formal dissolution of the USSR</a> in December 1991, the declaration of independence of <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">its constituent republics</a> and the collapse of communist governments across much of Africa and Asia. The United States was left as the world's only superpower.</dd></dl>
<ul><li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Digital_Revolution" title="Digital Revolution">Digital Revolution</a></i> (also known as the <i>Third Industrial Revolution</i>) is the shift from <a href="/wiki/Machine" title="Machine">mechanical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Analogue_electronics" title="Analogue electronics">analogue electronic</a> <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a> to <a href="/wiki/Digital_electronics" title="Digital electronics">digital electronics</a> which began in the latter half of the 20th century, with the adoption and proliferation of digital computers and digital record-keeping, that continues to the present day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> Implicitly, the term also refers to the sweeping changes brought about by digital <a href="/wiki/Computing" title="Computing">computing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communication" title="Communication">communication</a> <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technologies</a> during this period. From analogous to the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">Agricultural Revolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, the Digital Revolution marked the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Information_Age" title="Information Age">Information Age</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> Central to this revolution is the <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">mass production</a> and widespread use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_logic" title="Digital logic">digital logic</a>, <a href="/wiki/MOSFET" title="MOSFET">MOSFETs</a> (MOS <a href="/wiki/Transistor" title="Transistor">transistors</a>), <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">integrated circuit</a> (IC) chips, and their derived technologies, including <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microprocessor" title="Microprocessor">microprocessors</a>, digital <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cellular_phone" title="Cellular phone">cellular phones</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup>  These technological innovations have transformed traditional production and business techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Internet_age" title="Internet age">Internet Age</a></i> dates from late 1990, when Tim Berners-Lee invented <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a>, and created the world's first web page, marking the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a>.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_revolutions">Industrial revolutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Industrial revolutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Industrial_Revolution" title="Second Industrial Revolution">Second Industrial Revolution</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="760" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg/220px-Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg/330px-Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg/440px-Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>James Watt's steam engine</div></div></div>
<p>The development of the <a href="/wiki/Steam_engine" title="Steam engine">steam engine</a> started the Industrial Revolution in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Great Britain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> The steam engine was created to pump water from coal mines, enabling them to be deepened beyond <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">groundwater</a> levels. The date of the Industrial Revolution is not exact, but some studies suggest it occurred after the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>'s conquests of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mughal_Bengal" title="Mughal Bengal">Mughal Bengal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mysore" title="Kingdom of Mysore">Kingdom of Mysore</a> and the rest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mughal_India" title="Mughal India">India</a>, which were already observing the <a href="/wiki/Proto-industrialization" title="Proto-industrialization">proto-industrialization</a>. <a href="/wiki/Eric_Hobsbawm" title="Eric Hobsbawm">Eric Hobsbawm</a> held that it "broke out" in the 1780s and was not fully felt until the 1830s or 1840s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> while <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T.S._Ashton" title="T.S. Ashton">T.S. Ashton</a> held that it occurred roughly between 1760 and 1830 (in effect the reigns of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George III of the United Kingdom">George III</a>, The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_Regency" title="English Regency">Regency</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_IV_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George IV of the United Kingdom">George IV</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> The great changes of centuries before the 19th were more connected with ideas, religion or military conquest, and technological advance had only made small changes in the material wealth of ordinary people.
</p><p>The first Industrial Revolution merged into the Second Industrial Revolution around 1850, when technological and economic progress gained momentum with the development of steam-powered ships and railways, and later in the 19th century with the <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electric_power" title="Electric power">electric power</a> generation. The Second Industrial Revolution was a phase of the Industrial Revolution; labeled as the separate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technical_revolution" title="Technical revolution">Technical revolution</a>. From a technological and a social point of view there is no clean break between the two. Major innovations during the period occurred in the chemical, electrical, petroleum, and steel industries. Specific advancements included the introduction of oil fired steam turbine and internal combustion driven steel ships, the development of the airplane, the practical commercialization of the automobile, mass production of consumer goods, the perfection of canning, mechanical refrigeration and other <a href="/wiki/Food_preservation" title="Food preservation">food preservation</a> techniques, and the invention of the telephone.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrialization">Industrialization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Industrialization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AWA1936.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="814" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/AWA1936.jpg/220px-AWA1936.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/AWA1936.jpg/330px-AWA1936.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/AWA1936.jpg/440px-AWA1936.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AWA1936.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The late modern period saw extreme changes in the way people lived, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrialization" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a>.  This photo shows women working on parts at an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amalgamated_Wireless_(Australasia)" title="Amalgamated Wireless (Australasia)">AWA</a> factory in 1936, while men look on.</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrialization" title="Industrialization">Industrialization</a> is the process of social and economic change whereby a human group is transformed from a pre-industrial society into an industrial one. It is a subdivision of a more general <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modernization" title="Modernization">modernization</a> process, where <a href="/wiki/Social_change" title="Social change">social change</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a> are closely related with <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">technological innovation</a>, particularly with the development of large-scale energy and metallurgy production. It is the extensive organization of an economy for the purpose of manufacturing. Industrialization also introduces a form of philosophical change, where people obtain a different attitude towards <a href="/wiki/Nature" title="Nature">nature</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolution_in_manufacture_and_power">Revolution in manufacture and power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Revolution in manufacture and power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:First_passenger_railway_1830.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1315" data-file-width="1646" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/First_passenger_railway_1830.jpg/220px-First_passenger_railway_1830.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/First_passenger_railway_1830.jpg/330px-First_passenger_railway_1830.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/First_passenger_railway_1830.jpg/440px-First_passenger_railway_1830.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:First_passenger_railway_1830.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_and_Manchester_Railway" title="Liverpool and Manchester Railway">Liverpool and Manchester Railway</a> from 1830, world's first railway.</div></div></div>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Economic_system" title="Economic system">economy</a> based on <a href="/wiki/Manual_labour" title="Manual labour">manual labour</a> was replaced by one dominated by industry and the manufacture of machinery. It began with the mechanization of the <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textile</a> industries and the development of <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">iron</a>-making techniques, and trade expansion was enabled by the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Canal" title="Canal">canals</a>, improved roads, and then <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">railways</a>.
</p><p>The introduction of <a href="/wiki/Steam_engine" title="Steam engine">steam power</a> (fuelled primarily by <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>) and powered machinery (mainly in <a href="/wiki/Textile_manufacturing" title="Textile manufacturing">textile manufacturing</a>) underpinned the dramatic increases in production capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> The development of all-metal <a href="/wiki/Machine_tool" title="Machine tool">machine tools</a> in the first two decades of the 19th century facilitated the manufacture of more production machines for manufacturing in other industries.
</p><p>The modern <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry" title="Petroleum industry">petroleum industry</a> started in 1846 with the discovery of the process of refining <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a> from <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> by <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotian</a> <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Pineo_Gesner" title="Abraham Pineo Gesner">Abraham Pineo Gesner</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ignacy_%C5%81ukasiewicz" title="Ignacy Łukasiewicz">Ignacy Łukasiewicz</a> improved Gesner's method to develop a means of refining kerosene from the more readily available "rock oil" ("petr-oleum") <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seep" title="Seep">seeps</a> in 1852 and the first rock oil mine was built in <a href="/wiki/B%C3%B3brka,_Krosno_County" title="Bóbrka, Krosno County">Bóbrka</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Krosno" title="Krosno">Krosno</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galicia_(Central_Europe)" title="Galicia (Central Europe)">Galicia</a> in the following year. In 1854, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Silliman" title="Benjamin Silliman">Benjamin Silliman</a>, a science professor at <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">New Haven</a>, was the first to fractionate petroleum by distillation. These discoveries rapidly spread around the world.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_engineers">Notable engineers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Notable engineers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teslathinker.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1554" data-file-width="1206" decoding="async" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Teslathinker.jpg/150px-Teslathinker.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Teslathinker.jpg/225px-Teslathinker.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Teslathinker.jpg/299px-Teslathinker.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teslathinker.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nikola Tesla with his high-frequency transformer at East Houston Street, New York</div></div></div>
<p>Engineering achievements of the revolution ranged from electrification to developments in materials science. The advancements made a great contribution to the quality of life. In the first revolution, <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Paul" title="Lewis Paul">Lewis Paul</a> was the original inventor of roller spinning, the basis of the water frame for spinning cotton in a cotton mill. <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Boulton" title="Matthew Boulton">Matthew Boulton</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Watt" title="James Watt">James Watt</a>'s improvements to the steam engine were fundamental to the changes brought by the Industrial Revolution in both the Kingdom of Great Britain and the world.
</p><p>In the latter part of the second revolution, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_Alva_Edison" title="Thomas Alva Edison">Thomas Alva Edison</a> developed many devices that greatly influenced life around the world and is often credited with the creation of the first industrial research laboratory. In 1882, Edison switched on the world's first large-scale <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_supply_network" title="Electrical supply network">electrical supply network</a> that provided 110 volts direct current to fifty-nine customers in lower Manhattan. Also toward the end of the second industrial revolution, <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Tesla" title="Nikola Tesla">Nikola Tesla</a> made many contributions in the field of <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magnetism" title="Magnetism">magnetism</a> in the late 19th and early 20th centuries.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_effects_and_classes">Social effects and classes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Social effects and classes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Industrial Revolutions were major <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technological</a>, <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomics" title="Socioeconomics">socioeconomic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">cultural</a> changes in late 18th and early 19th centuries that began in Britain and spread throughout the world. The effects spread throughout Western Europe and North America during the 19th century, eventually affecting the majority of the world. The impact of this change on <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">society</a> was enormous and is often compared to the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">Neolithic Revolution</a>, when mankind developed <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> and gave up its <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> lifestyle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>It has been argued that <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> per capita was much more stable and progressed at a much slower rate until the industrial revolution and the emergence of the modern <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> economy, and that it has since increased rapidly in capitalist countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mid-19th-century_European_revolts">Mid-19th-century European revolts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Mid-19th-century European revolts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alexanderplatz_Berlin_1848.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Alexanderplatz_Berlin_1848.jpg/220px-Alexanderplatz_Berlin_1848.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Alexanderplatz_Berlin_1848.jpg/330px-Alexanderplatz_Berlin_1848.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Alexanderplatz_Berlin_1848.jpg/440px-Alexanderplatz_Berlin_1848.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alexanderplatz_Berlin_1848.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">German Revolution</a>, Berlin 1848</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">European Revolutions of 1848</a>, known in some countries as the Spring of Nations or the Year of Revolution, were a series of political upheavals throughout the European continent. Described as a revolutionary wave, the period of unrest began in France and then, further propelled by the French Revolution of 1848, soon spread to the rest of Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> Although most of the revolutions were quickly put down, there was a significant amount of violence in many areas, with tens of thousands of people tortured and killed. While the immediate political effects of the revolutions were reversed, the long-term reverberations of the events were far-reaching.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_age_reformism">Industrial age reformism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Industrial age reformism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Industrial age <a href="/wiki/Reform_movement" title="Reform movement">reform movements</a> began the gradual change of society rather than with episodes of rapid fundamental changes. The reformists' ideas were often grounded in liberalism, although they also possessed aspects of utopian, socialist or religious concepts. The Radical movement campaigned for electoral reform, a reform of the Poor Laws, free trade, educational reform, postal reform, prison reform, and public sanitation.
</p><p>Following the Enlightenment's ideas, the reformers looked to the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_Revolution" title="Scientific Revolution">Scientific Revolution</a> and industrial progress to solve the social problems which arose with the Industrial Revolution. Newton's natural philosophy combined a mathematics of axiomatic proof with the mechanics of physical observation, yielding a coherent system of verifiable predictions and replacing a previous reliance on revelation and inspired truth. Applied to public life, this approach yielded several successful campaigns for changes in social policy.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_Russia">Imperial Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Imperial Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Peasant_Girls-retouched.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1436" data-file-width="1660" decoding="async" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Russian_Peasant_Girls-retouched.jpg/220px-Russian_Peasant_Girls-retouched.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Russian_Peasant_Girls-retouched.jpg/330px-Russian_Peasant_Girls-retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Russian_Peasant_Girls-retouched.jpg/440px-Russian_Peasant_Girls-retouched.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Peasant_Girls-retouched.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Russian Peasant Girls, 1900</div></div></div>
<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a>, Russia was proclaimed an Empire in 1721 and became recognized as a world power. Ruling from 1682 to 1725, Peter defeated Sweden in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">Great Northern War</a>, forcing it to cede West <a href="/wiki/Karelia" title="Karelia">Karelia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ingria" title="Ingria">Ingria</a> (two regions lost by Russia in the <a href="/wiki/Time_of_Troubles" title="Time of Troubles">Time of Troubles</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Governorate_of_Estonia" title="Governorate of Estonia">Estland</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Livland" title="Livland">Livland</a>, securing Russia's access to the sea and sea trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> On the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> Peter founded a new capital called <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>, later known as Russia's <i>Window to Europe</i>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great%27s_reforms" title="Peter the Great's reforms">Peter the Great's reforms</a> brought considerable Western European cultural influences to Russia. <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine II</a> (<i>the Great</i>), who ruled in 1762–96, extended Russian political control over the Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth and incorporated most of its territories into Russia during the <a href="/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland" title="Partitions of Poland">Partitions of Poland</a>, pushing the Russian frontier westward and southward.  Russia would <a href="/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_Siberia" title="Russian conquest of Siberia">colonize</a> the vast Asian lands of <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> expanding by land to the Pacific Coast of Asia, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">North America</a>.  As the large realm embraced <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">Absolute Monarchy</a> Russia remained more conservative than its western neighbors. In the 19th century, Russia was invaded by France in 1812 but emerged as a more powerful superpower afterwards. Nonetheless, industrialization did not come to Russia until the 1870s. The Medieval practice of serfdom was <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_reform_of_1861" title="Emancipation reform of 1861">abolished</a> in 1861 freeing over thirty million Russian peasants. A market economy finally emerged in the Russian Empire. However class warfare rose, and the nation was vulnerable due to rivalries with the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese Empire</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonization of the Americas</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_Independence_(1819),_by_John_Trumbull.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1970" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg/220px-Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg/330px-Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg/440px-Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_Independence_(1819),_by_John_Trumbull.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Trumbull" title="John Trumbull">John Trumbull</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_(Trumbull)" title="Declaration of Independence (Trumbull)">Declaration of Independence</a></i>, showing the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Five" title="Committee of Five">Committee of Five</a> in charge of drafting the Declaration in 1776 as it presents its work to the <a href="/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress" title="Second Continental Congress">Second Continental Congress</a> in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_Wars" title="French and Indian Wars">French and Indian Wars</a> were a series of conflicts in North America that represented the actions there that accompanied the European dynastic wars. In Quebec, the wars are generally referred to as the Intercolonial Wars. While some conflicts involved Spanish and Dutch forces, all pitted Great Britain, its colonies and American Indian allies on one side and France, its colonies and Indian allies on the other.
</p><p>The expanding French and British colonies were contending for control of the western, or interior, territories. Whenever the European countries went to war, there were actions within and by these colonies although the dates of the conflict did not necessarily exactly coincide with those of the larger conflicts.
</p><p>Beginning the Age of Revolution, the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> and the ensuing political upheaval during the last half of the 18th century saw the Thirteen Colonies of North America overthrow the governance of the Parliament of Great Britain, and then reject the British monarchy itself to become the sovereign United States of America. In this period the colonies first rejected the authority of the Parliament to govern them without representation, and formed self-governing independent states. The Second Continental Congress then joined together against the British to defend that self-governance in the armed conflict from 1775 to 1783 known as the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> (also called American War of Independence).
</p><p>The American Revolution began with fighting at Lexington and Concord. On July 4, 1776, they issued the Declaration of Independence, which proclaimed their independence from Great Britain and their formation of a cooperative union. In June 1776, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">Benjamin Franklin</a> was appointed a member of the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Five" title="Committee of Five">Committee of Five</a> that drafted the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a>. Although he was temporarily disabled by gout and unable to attend most meetings of the Committee, Franklin made several small changes to the draft sent to him by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a>.
</p><p>The rebellious states defeated Great Britain in the American Revolutionary War, the first successful colonial war of independence. While the states had already rejected the governance of Parliament, through the Declaration the new United States now rejected the legitimacy of the monarchy to demand allegiance. The war raged for seven years, with effective American victory, followed by formal British abandonment of any claim to the United States with the Treaty of Paris.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Convention" title="Philadelphia Convention">Philadelphia Convention</a> in 1787 set up the current United States; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a> ratification the following year made the states part of a single republic with a limited central government. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Bill_of_Rights" title="United States Bill of Rights">Bill of Rights</a>, comprising ten constitutional amendments guaranteeing many fundamental civil rights and freedoms, was ratified in 1791.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_dominance_and_the_19th_century">European dominance and the 19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: European dominance and the 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/19th_century" title="19th century">19th century</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_relations_(1814%E2%80%931919)" title="International relations (1814–1919)">International relations (1814–1919)</a></div>
<p>Historians define the 19th century <a href="/wiki/List_of_time_periods" title="List of time periods">historical era</a> as stretching from 1815 (the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>) to 1914 (the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>). Alternatively, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Hobsbawm" title="Eric Hobsbawm">Eric Hobsbawm</a> defined the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_long_19th_century" title="The long 19th century">"Long Nineteenth Century"</a> as spanning the years 1789 to 1914.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperialism_and_empires">Imperialism and empires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Imperialism and empires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">Imperialism</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chronology_of_Western_colonialism" title="Chronology of Western colonialism">Chronology of Western colonialism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Imperalism.xcf"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Imperalism.xcf/220px-Imperalism.xcf.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Imperalism.xcf/330px-Imperalism.xcf.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Imperalism.xcf/440px-Imperalism.xcf.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Imperalism.xcf" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Montage of paintings that depict European wars of imperialism. By clockwise, wars include <a href="/wiki/French_conquest_of_Algeria" title="French conquest of Algeria">French Algerian War</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">Opium War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_Central_Asia" title="Russian conquest of Central Asia">Russian Conquest of Central Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Zulu_War" title="Anglo-Zulu War">Zulu War</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the 1800s and early 1900s, once great and powerful Empires such as Spain, Ottoman Turkey, the Mughal Empire, and the Kingdom of Portugal began to break apart. Spain, which was at one time unrivaled in Europe, had been declining for a long time when it was crippled by Napoleon Bonaparte's invasion. Sensing the time was right, Spain's vast colonies in South America began a series of rebellions that ended with almost all of the Spanish territories gaining their independence.
</p><p>The once mighty Ottoman Empire was wracked with a series of revolutions, resulting with the Ottoman's only holding a small region that surrounded the capital, Istanbul.
</p><p>The Mughal empire, which was descended from the Mongol Khanate, was bested by the upcoming <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maratha_Confederacy" title="Maratha Confederacy">Maratha Confederacy</a>. All was going well for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maratha" title="Maratha">Marathas</a> until the British took an interest in the riches of India and the British ended up ruling not just the boundaries of Modern India, but also Pakistan, Burma, Nepal, Bangladesh and some Southern Regions of Afghanistan.
</p><p>The King of Portugal's vast territory of Brazil reformed into the independent Empire of Brazil. With the defeat of Napoleonic France, Britain became undoubtedly the most powerful country in the world, and by the end of the First World War controlled a Quarter of the world's population and a third of its surface. However, the power of the British Empire did not end on land, since it had the greatest navy on the planet. Electricity, steel, and petroleum enabled Germany to become a great <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_(international)" title="Power (international)">international power</a> that raced to create empires of its own.
</p><p>Substantial <a href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_the_Americas" title="Decolonization of the Americas">decolonization of the Americas</a> occurred through various revolutions and wars of independence fought by new countries in the Americans against European colonizers in late 18th and early-to-mid-19th centuries. The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a> lasted from 1808 until 1829, directly related to the Napoleonic French invasion of Spain. The conflict started with short-lived governing juntas established in Chuquisaca and Quito opposing the composition of the Supreme Central Junta of Seville. When the Central Junta fell to the French, numerous new Juntas appeared all across the Americas, eventually resulting in a chain of newly independent countries stretching from Argentina and Chile in the south, to Mexico in the north. After the death of the king Ferdinand VII, in 1833, only Cuba and Puerto Rico remained under Spanish rule, until the Spanish–American War in 1898. Unlike the Spanish, the Portuguese did not divide their colonial territory in America. The captaincies they created were subdued to a centralized administration in Salvador (later relocated to Rio de Janeiro) which reported directly to the Portuguese Crown until its independence in 1822, becoming the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Meiji_Restoration" title="Meiji Restoration">Meiji Restoration</a> was a chain of events that led to enormous changes in Japan's political and social structure that was taking a firm hold at the beginning of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meiji_Era" title="Meiji Era">Meiji Era</a> which coincided the opening of Japan by the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Ships" title="Black Ships">Black Ships</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commodore_(USN)" title="Commodore (USN)">Commodore</a> <a href="/wiki/Matthew_C._Perry" title="Matthew C. Perry">Matthew Perry</a> and made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Japan" title="Imperial Japan">Imperial Japan</a> a <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great power</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Russia" title="Imperial Russia">Russia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing Dynasty</a> China failed to keep pace with the other world powers which led to massive social unrest in both empires. The Qing Dynasty's military power weakened during the 19th century, and faced with international pressure, massive <a href="/wiki/Rebellion" title="Rebellion">rebellions</a> and defeats in wars, the dynasty declined after the mid-19th century.
</p><p>European powers controlled parts of Oceania, with French <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a> from 1853 and <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a> from 1889; the Germans established colonies in <a href="/wiki/German_New_Guinea" title="German New Guinea">New Guinea</a> in 1884, and <a href="/wiki/German_Samoa" title="German Samoa">Samoa</a> in 1900. The United States expanded into the Pacific with Hawaii becoming a <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Hawaii" title="Territory of Hawaii">U.S. territory</a> from 1898. Disagreements between the US, Germany and UK over Samoa led to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tripartite_Convention_(1899)" title="Tripartite Convention (1899)">Tripartite Convention of 1899</a>.
</p>
