<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Victorian_era">British Victorian era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: British Victorian era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_Empire_1897.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="849" data-file-width="1116" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/British_Empire_1897.jpg/220px-British_Empire_1897.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/British_Empire_1897.jpg/330px-British_Empire_1897.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/British_Empire_1897.jpg/440px-British_Empire_1897.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_Empire_1897.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The British Empire in 1897, marked in the traditional colour for imperial British dominions on maps</div></div></div>
<p>The Victorian era of the United Kingdom was the period of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>'s reign from June 1837 to January 1901. This was a long period of prosperity for the British people, as profits gained from the overseas British Empire, as well as from industrial improvements at home, allowed a large, educated middle class to develop. Some scholars would extend the beginning of the period—as defined by a variety of sensibilities and political games that have come to be associated with the Victorians—back five years to the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Reform_Act_1832" title="Reform Act 1832">Reform Act 1832</a>.
In Britain's "imperial century",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> victory over Napoleon left Britain without any serious international rival, other than Russia in central Asia. Unchallenged at sea, Britain adopted the role of global policeman, a state of affairs later known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Pax_Britannica" title="Pax Britannica">Pax Britannica</a></i>, and a foreign policy of "<a href="/wiki/Splendid_isolation" title="Splendid isolation">splendid isolation</a>". Alongside the formal control it exerted over its own colonies, Britain's dominant position in world trade meant that it effectively controlled the economies of many nominally independent countries, such as China, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Siam</a>, which has been generally characterized as "<a href="/wiki/Informal_empire" title="Informal empire">informal empire</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> Of note during this time was the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Zulu_War" title="Anglo-Zulu War">Anglo-Zulu War</a>, which was fought in 1879 between the British Empire and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zulu_Empire" title="Zulu Empire">Zulu Empire</a>.
</p><p>British imperial strength was underpinned by the <a href="/wiki/Steamboat" title="Steamboat">steamship</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Telegraphy" title="Telegraphy">telegraph</a>, new technologies invented in the second half of the 19th century, allowing it to control and defend the Empire. By 1902, the British Empire was linked together by a network of telegraph cables, the so-called <a href="/wiki/All_Red_Line" title="All Red Line">All Red Line</a>. Growing until 1922, around 13,000,000 square miles (34,000,000 km<sup>2</sup>) of territory and roughly 458 million people were added to the British Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> The British established colonies in Australia in 1788, New Zealand in 1840 and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_Fiji" title="Colonial Fiji">Fiji</a> in 1872, with much of <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a> becoming part of the British Empire.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_governments_and_conflicts">French governments and conflicts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: French governments and conflicts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Restoration_in_France" title="Bourbon Restoration in France">Bourbon Restoration</a> followed the ousting of Napoleon I of France in 1814. The Allies restored the Bourbon Dynasty to the French throne. The ensuing period is called the Restoration, following French usage, and is characterized by a sharp conservative reaction and the re-establishment of the Roman Catholic Church as a power in French politics. The <a href="/wiki/July_Monarchy" title="July Monarchy">July Monarchy</a> was a period of liberal constitutional monarchy in France under King Louis-Philippe starting with the July Revolution (or Three Glorious Days) of 1830 and ending with the Revolution of 1848. The <a href="/wiki/Second_French_Empire" title="Second French Empire">Second Empire</a> was the Imperial Bonapartist regime of Napoleon III from 1852 to 1870, between the Second Republic and the Third Republic, in France.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BismarckundNapoleonIII.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1053" data-file-width="1516" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/BismarckundNapoleonIII.jpg/220px-BismarckundNapoleonIII.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/BismarckundNapoleonIII.jpg/330px-BismarckundNapoleonIII.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/BismarckundNapoleonIII.jpg/440px-BismarckundNapoleonIII.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BismarckundNapoleonIII.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_III_of_France" title="Napoleon III of France">Napoleon III</a> and <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck" title="Otto von Bismarck">Bismarck</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sedan" title="Battle of Sedan">Battle of Sedan</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a> was a conflict between France and Prussia, while Prussia was backed up by the North German Confederation, of which it was a member, and the South German states of Baden, Württemberg and Bavaria. The complete Prussian and German victory brought about the final unification of Germany under King Wilhelm I of Prussia. It also marked the downfall of Napoleon III and the end of the Second French Empire, which was replaced by the Third Republic. As part of the settlement, almost all of the territory of Alsace-Lorraine was taken by Prussia to become a part of Germany, which it would retain until the end of World War I.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">French Third Republic</a> was the republican government of France between the end of the Second French Empire following the defeat of Louis-Napoléon in the Franco-Prussian war in 1870 and the Vichy Regime after the invasion of France by the German Third Reich in 1940. The Third Republic endured seventy years, making it the most long-lasting regime in France since the collapse of the Ancien Régime in the French Revolution of 1789.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italian_unification">Italian unification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Italian unification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gioacchino_toma_roma_o_morte_1863.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="565" data-file-width="550" decoding="async" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Gioacchino_toma_roma_o_morte_1863.jpg/220px-Gioacchino_toma_roma_o_morte_1863.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Gioacchino_toma_roma_o_morte_1863.jpg/330px-Gioacchino_toma_roma_o_morte_1863.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Gioacchino_toma_roma_o_morte_1863.jpg/440px-Gioacchino_toma_roma_o_morte_1863.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gioacchino_toma_roma_o_morte_1863.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Rome or Death</i>, Italian patriotic painting by <a href="/wiki/Gioacchino_Toma" title="Gioacchino Toma">Gioacchino Toma</a>, 1863</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">Italian unification</a> was the political and social movement that annexed different states of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_peninsula" title="Italian peninsula">Italian peninsula</a> into the single state of Italy in the 19th century. There is a lack of consensus on the exact dates for the beginning and the end of this period, but many scholars agree that the process began with the end of Napoleonic rule and the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> in 1815, and approximately ended with the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a> in 1871, though the last <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italia_irredenta" title="Italia irredenta">città irredente</a></i> did not join the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a> until after World War I.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slavery_and_abolition">Slavery and abolition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Slavery and abolition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Une_Dame_d%C2%B4une_Fortune_Ordinaire_dans_son_Int%C3%A9rieur_au_Milieu_de_ses_Habitudes_Journali%C3%A8res,_by_Jean-Baptiste_Debret_1823.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3381" data-file-width="4717" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Une_Dame_d%C2%B4une_Fortune_Ordinaire_dans_son_Int%C3%A9rieur_au_Milieu_de_ses_Habitudes_Journali%C3%A8res%2C_by_Jean-Baptiste_Debret_1823.jpg/220px-Une_Dame_d%C2%B4une_Fortune_Ordinaire_dans_son_Int%C3%A9rieur_au_Milieu_de_ses_Habitudes_Journali%C3%A8res%2C_by_Jean-Baptiste_Debret_1823.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Une_Dame_d%C2%B4une_Fortune_Ordinaire_dans_son_Int%C3%A9rieur_au_Milieu_de_ses_Habitudes_Journali%C3%A8res%2C_by_Jean-Baptiste_Debret_1823.jpg/330px-Une_Dame_d%C2%B4une_Fortune_Ordinaire_dans_son_Int%C3%A9rieur_au_Milieu_de_ses_Habitudes_Journali%C3%A8res%2C_by_Jean-Baptiste_Debret_1823.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Une_Dame_d%C2%B4une_Fortune_Ordinaire_dans_son_Int%C3%A9rieur_au_Milieu_de_ses_Habitudes_Journali%C3%A8res%2C_by_Jean-Baptiste_Debret_1823.jpg/440px-Une_Dame_d%C2%B4une_Fortune_Ordinaire_dans_son_Int%C3%A9rieur_au_Milieu_de_ses_Habitudes_Journali%C3%A8res%2C_by_Jean-Baptiste_Debret_1823.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Une_Dame_d%C2%B4une_Fortune_Ordinaire_dans_son_Int%C3%A9rieur_au_Milieu_de_ses_Habitudes_Journali%C3%A8res,_by_Jean-Baptiste_Debret_1823.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Depiction of <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slavery</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, before 1823</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism" title="Abolitionism">Abolitionism</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slavery</a> was greatly reduced around the world in the 19th century. Following a successful <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">slave revolt in Haiti</a>, Britain forced the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a> to halt their practice of kidnapping and enslaving Europeans, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavery_Abolition_Act" title="Slavery Abolition Act">banned slavery throughout its domain</a>, and charged its navy with ending the global <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a>. Slavery was then abolished in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emancipation_reform_of_1861_in_Russia" title="Emancipation reform of 1861 in Russia">Russia</a>(1861), <a href="/wiki/Thirteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Thirteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">America</a>(1865), and <a href="/wiki/Lei_%C3%81urea" title="Lei Áurea">Brazil</a>(1888).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="African_colonization">African colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: African colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Colonisation_of_Africa" title="Colonisation of Africa">Colonisation of Africa</a></div>
<p>Following the abolition of the slave trade in 1807 and propelled by economic exploitation, the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a> was initiated formally at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berlin_West_Africa_Conference" title="Berlin West Africa Conference">Berlin West Africa Conference</a> in 1884–1885. The Berlin Conference attempted to avoid war among the European powers by allowing the European rival countries to carve up the continent of Africa into national colonies. Africans were not consulted.
</p><p>The major European powers laid claim to the areas of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> where they could exhibit a sphere of influence over the area. These claims did not have to have any substantial land holdings or treaties to be legitimate. The European power that demonstrated its control over a territory accepted the mandate to rule that region as a national <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a>. The European nation that held the claim developed and benefited from their colony's commercial interests without having to fear rival European competition. With the colonial claim came the underlying assumption that the European power that exerted control would use its mandate to offer protection and provide welfare for its colonial peoples, however, this principle remained more theory than practice. There were many documented instances of material and moral conditions deteriorating for native Africans in the late nineteenth and early twentieth centuries under European colonial rule, to the point where the colonial experience for them has been described as "hell on earth."
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kongokonferenz.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2790" data-file-width="3631" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Kongokonferenz.jpg/220px-Kongokonferenz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Kongokonferenz.jpg/330px-Kongokonferenz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Kongokonferenz.jpg/440px-Kongokonferenz.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kongokonferenz.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>European officials staking claims to <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a></div></div></div>
<p>At the time of the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a>, Africa contained one-fifth of the world's population living in one-quarter of the world's land area. However, from Europe's perspective, they were dividing an unknown continent. European countries established a few coastal colonies in Africa by the mid-nineteenth century, which included <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a> (Great Britain), <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> (Portugal), and <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> (France), but until the late nineteenth century Europe largely traded with free African states without feeling the need for territorial possession. Until the 1880s most of Africa remained uncharted, with western maps from the period generally showing blank spaces for the continent's interior.
</p><p>From the 1880s to 1914, the European powers expanded their control across the African continent, competing with each other for Africa's land and resources. <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> controlled various colonial holdings in East Africa that spanned the length of the African continent from Egypt in the north to South Africa. The <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> gained major ground in West Africa, and the <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> held colonies in southern Africa. <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> established a small number of colonies at various points throughout the continent, which included German East Africa (Tanganyika) and German Southwest Africa for Germany, Eritrea and Libya for Italy, and the Canary Islands and Rio de Oro in northwestern Africa for Spain. Finally, for <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="Leopold II of Belgium">King Leopold</a> (ruled from 1865 to 1909), there was the large “piece of that great African cake” known as the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Congo</a>, which became his personal fiefdom. By 1914, almost the entire continent was under European control. <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>, which was settled by freed American slaves in the 1820s, and Abyssinia (<a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>) in eastern Africa were the last remaining independent African states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Meiji_Japan">Meiji Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Meiji Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meiji_period" title="Meiji period">Meiji period</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:View_of_Kobe_LACMA_M.91.377.8.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1617" data-file-width="2100" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/View_of_Kobe_LACMA_M.91.377.8.jpg/220px-View_of_Kobe_LACMA_M.91.377.8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/View_of_Kobe_LACMA_M.91.377.8.jpg/330px-View_of_Kobe_LACMA_M.91.377.8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/View_of_Kobe_LACMA_M.91.377.8.jpg/440px-View_of_Kobe_LACMA_M.91.377.8.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:View_of_Kobe_LACMA_M.91.377.8.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kobe Japan and its harbor, 1865. Hand colored.</div></div></div><p> Around the end of the 19th century and into the 20th century, the <a href="/wiki/Meiji_era" title="Meiji era">Meiji era</a> occurred during the reign of the <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Meiji" title="Emperor Meiji">Meiji Emperor</a>. During this time, Japan started its modernization and rose to world power status. This <a href="/wiki/Japanese_era_name" title="Japanese era name">era name</a> means "Enlightened Rule". In Japan, the Meiji Restoration started in the 1860s, marking the rapid modernization by the Japanese themselves along European lines. Much research has focused on the issues of discontinuity versus continuity with the previous Tokugawa Period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> It was not until the beginning of the Meiji Era that the Japanese government began taking modernization seriously. Japan expanded its military production base by opening arsenals in various locations. The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_War_(pre-modern_Japan)" title="Ministry of War (pre-modern Japan)">hyobusho</a> (war office) was replaced with a <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army" title="Imperial Japanese Army">War Department</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Navy" title="Imperial Japanese Navy">Naval Department.</a> The <a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">samurai</a> class suffered great disappointment the following years.
</p><p>Laws were instituted that required every able-bodied male Japanese citizen, regardless of class, to serve a mandatory term of three years with the first reserves and two additional years with the second reserves. This action, the deathblow for the samurai warriors and their <i>daimyōs</i>, initially met resistance from both the peasant and warrior alike. The peasant class interpreted the term for military service, ketsu-eki ("blood tax") literally, and attempted to avoid service by any means necessary. The Japanese government began modelling their ground forces after the French military. The French government contributed greatly to the training of Japanese officers. Many were employed at the military academy in Kyoto, and many more still were feverishly translating French field manuals for use in the Japanese ranks. Japan's modernized military gave Japan the opportunity to engage in Imperialism with its victory against the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing Empire</a> in the <a href="/wiki/First_Sino-Japanese_War" title="First Sino-Japanese War">First Sino-Japanese War</a> Japan annexed <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_under_Japanese_rule" title="Taiwan under Japanese rule">Taiwan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korea_under_Japanese_rule" title="Korea under Japanese rule">Korea</a> and the Chinese province of <a href="/wiki/Shandong" title="Shandong">Shandong</a>.
</p><p>After the death of the Meiji Emperor, the <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Taish%C5%8D" title="Emperor Taishō">Taishō Emperor</a> took the throne, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taish%C5%8D_period" title="Taishō period">Taishō period</a> was a time of democratic reform granting democratic rights to all Japanese men. Foreigners would be instrumental in aiding in Japan's modernization.  A key foreign observer of the remarkable and rapid changes in <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Japan" title="Culture of Japan">Japanese society</a> in this period was <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Mason_Satow" title="Ernest Mason Satow">Ernest Mason Satow</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_(1865%E2%80%931918)" title="History of the United States (1865–1918)">History of the United States (1865–1918)</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_North_America_since_1763" title="Territorial evolution of North America since 1763">Territorial evolution of North America since 1763</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Colonial_history_of_the_United_States" title="Colonial history of the United States">Colonial history of the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Indian_Wars" title="American Indian Wars">American Indian Wars</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States#19th_century" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native Americans in the United States § 19th century</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antebellum_expansion">Antebellum expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Antebellum expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/American_frontier" title="American frontier">American frontier</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territorial_changes_of_the_United_States" title="Territorial changes of the United States">Territorial changes of the United States</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Westward_the_Course_of_Empire.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="402" data-file-width="528" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Westward_the_Course_of_Empire.jpg/220px-Westward_the_Course_of_Empire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Westward_the_Course_of_Empire.jpg/330px-Westward_the_Course_of_Empire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Westward_the_Course_of_Empire.jpg/440px-Westward_the_Course_of_Empire.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Westward_the_Course_of_Empire.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>American westward expansion is idealized in <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Leutze" title="Emanuel Leutze">Emanuel Leutze</a>'s famous painting <i>Westward the Course of Empire Takes its Way</i> (1861).</div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antebellum_Age" title="Antebellum Age">Antebellum Age</a> was a period of increasing division in the country based on the growth of slavery in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">American South</a> and in the western territories of <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a> that eventually led to the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a> in 1861. The Antebellum Period is often considered to have begun with the <a href="/wiki/Kansas%E2%80%93Nebraska_Act" title="Kansas–Nebraska Act">Kansas–Nebraska Act</a> of 1854,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> although it may have begun as early as 1812. This period is also significant because it marked the transition of American manufacturing to the industrial revolution.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>"<a href="/wiki/Manifest_destiny" title="Manifest destiny">Manifest destiny</a>" was the belief that the United States was destined to expand across the North American continent, from the Atlantic seaboard to the Pacific Ocean. During this time, the United States expanded to the Pacific Ocean—"from sea to shining sea"—largely defining the borders of the contiguous United States as they are today.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War_and_Reconstruction">Civil War and Reconstruction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Civil War and Reconstruction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><audio class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="110" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Gettysburg_by_Britton.ogg" id="mwe_player_0" preload="none" style="width:220px;" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="130787" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (131 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a1/Gettysburg_by_Britton.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="220752" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/a/a1/Gettysburg_by_Britton.ogg/Gettysburg_by_Britton.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/></audio> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gettysburg_by_Britton.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Modern recording of <a href="/wiki/Gettysburg_Address" title="Gettysburg Address">Gettysburg Address</a> originally spoken by <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S President</a> <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden_0.5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3500" data-file-width="4828" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden_0.5.jpg/220px-Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden_0.5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden_0.5.jpg/330px-Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden_0.5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden_0.5.jpg/440px-Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden_0.5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden_0.5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gettysburg" title="Battle of Gettysburg">Battle of Gettysburg</a> – Restoration by Adam Cuerden 0.5</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era" title="Reconstruction era">Reconstruction era</a></div>
<p>The American Civil War began when seven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_state" title="Slave state">Southern slave states</a> declared their <a href="/wiki/Secession" title="Secession">secession</a> from the U.S. and formed the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate States of America</a>, the Confederacy (four more states joined the Confederacy later). Led by <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Davis" title="Jefferson Davis">Jefferson Davis</a>, they fought against the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">U.S. federal government (the Union)</a> under President <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a>, which was supported by all the free states and the five <a href="/wiki/Border_states_(American_Civil_War)" title="Border states (American Civil War)">border slave states</a> in the north.
</p><p>Northern leaders agreed that victory would require more than the end of fighting. Secession and Confederate nationalism had to be totally repudiated and all forms of slavery or quasi-slavery had to be eliminated. Lincoln proved effective in mobilizing support for the war goals, raising large armies and supplying them, avoiding foreign interference, and making the end of slavery a war goal. The Confederacy had a larger area than it could defend, and it failed to keep its ports open and its rivers clear as was the case in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Vicksburg" title="Siege of Vicksburg">Battle of Vicksburg</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">North</a> kept up the pressure as the South could barely feed and clothe its soldiers. Its soldiers, especially those in the East under the command of General <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">Robert E. Lee</a> proved highly resourceful until they finally were overwhelmed by Generals <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Ulysses S. Grant</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Tecumseh_Sherman" title="William Tecumseh Sherman">William T. Sherman</a> in 1864–65. The <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era" title="Reconstruction era">Reconstruction Era</a> (1863–77) began with the <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_Proclamation" title="Emancipation Proclamation">Emancipation proclamation</a> in 1863, and included freedom, full citizenship and voting rights for Southern blacks. It was followed by a reaction that left the blacks in a second class status legally, politically, socially and economically until the 1960s.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Gilded_Age_and_legacy">The Gilded Age and legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: The Gilded Age and legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gilded_Age" title="Gilded Age">Gilded Age</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><video class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="63" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Flatiron_Building_and_Street_Scene_October_8th_1902_New_York_City.ogv" height="165" id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Flatiron_Building_and_Street_Scene_October_8th_1902_New_York_City.ogv/220px--Flatiron_Building_and_Street_Scene_October_8th_1902_New_York_City.ogv.jpg" preload="none" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="253864" data-framerate="29.97002997003" data-height="240" data-shorttitle="WebM 240P" data-title="Small WebM (240P)" data-transcodekey="240p.webm" data-width="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/2d/Flatiron_Building_and_Street_Scene_October_8th_1902_New_York_City.ogv/Flatiron_Building_and_Street_Scene_October_8th_1902_New_York_City.ogv.240p.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp8, vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="164528" data-framerate="29.97002997003" data-height="180" data-shorttitle="VP9 180P" data-title="Low bandwidth VP9 (180P)" data-transcodekey="180p.vp9.webm" data-width="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/2d/Flatiron_Building_and_Street_Scene_October_8th_1902_New_York_City.ogv/Flatiron_Building_and_Street_Scene_October_8th_1902_New_York_City.ogv.180p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/></video> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flatiron_Building_and_Street_Scene_October_8th_1902_New_York_City.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1902 New York City in early <a href="/wiki/Skyscraper" title="Skyscraper">skyscrapers</a></div></div></div>
<p>During the Gilded Age, there was substantial growth in population in the United States and extravagant displays of wealth and excess of America's upper-class during the post-Civil War and post-Reconstruction era, in the late 19th century. The wealth polarization derived primarily from industrial and population expansion. The businessmen of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Industrial_Revolution" title="Second Industrial Revolution">Second Industrial Revolution</a> created industrial towns and cities in the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">Northeast</a> with new factories, and contributed to the creation of an ethnically diverse industrial <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">working class</a> which produced the wealth owned by rising super-rich <a href="/wiki/Robber_baron_(industrialist)" title="Robber baron (industrialist)">industrialists and financiers called the "robber barons"</a>. An example is the company of <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">John D. Rockefeller</a>, who was an important figure in shaping the new oil industry. Using highly effective tactics and aggressive practices, later widely criticized, <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a> absorbed or destroyed most of its competition.
</p><p>The creation of a modern industrial economy took place. With the creation of a <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">transportation and communication infrastructure</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Corporation" title="Corporation">corporation</a> became the dominant form of business organization and a <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">managerial revolution</a> transformed <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">business</a> operations. In 1890, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_United_States" title="Congress of the United States">Congress</a> passed the <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Antitrust_Act" title="Sherman Antitrust Act">Sherman Antitrust Act</a>—the source of all American anti-monopoly laws. The law forbade every contract, scheme, deal, or conspiracy to restrain trade, though the phrase "restraint of trade" remained subjective. By the beginning of the 20th century, per capita income and <a href="/wiki/Industrial_production" title="Industrial production">industrial production</a> in the United States exceeded that of any other country except Britain. Long hours and hazardous working conditions led many workers to attempt to form <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labor_union" title="Labor union">labor unions</a> despite strong opposition from industrialists and the courts. But the courts did protect the marketplace, declaring the Standard Oil group to be an "unreasonable" <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">monopoly</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Antitrust_Act" title="Sherman Antitrust Act">Sherman Antitrust Act</a> in 1911. It ordered Standard to break up into 34 independent companies with different boards of directors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_philosophy">Science and philosophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Science and philosophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><audio class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="299" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Liszt-_au_bord_d_une.ogg" id="mwe_player_2" preload="none" style="width:220px;" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="137700" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (138 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/40/Liszt-_au_bord_d_une.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="198576" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/40/Liszt-_au_bord_d_une.ogg/Liszt-_au_bord_d_une.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/></audio> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Liszt-_au_bord_d_une.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An example of 19th century <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">Classical Music</a> Liszt- au bord d une, 1855</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Darwin%27s_finches_by_Gould.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1319" data-file-width="1748" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Darwin%27s_finches_by_Gould.jpg/220px-Darwin%27s_finches_by_Gould.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Darwin%27s_finches_by_Gould.jpg/330px-Darwin%27s_finches_by_Gould.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Darwin%27s_finches_by_Gould.jpg/440px-Darwin%27s_finches_by_Gould.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Darwin%27s_finches_by_Gould.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Charles Darwin's finches by Gould, 1882. <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a> used the example of <a href="/wiki/Darwin%27s_finches" title="Darwin's finches">finches</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">Galapagos Islands</a> as evidence for the <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">Theory of Evolution</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Replacing the <a href="/wiki/Classical_physics" title="Classical physics">classical physics</a> in use since the end of the scientific revolution, <i><a href="/wiki/Modern_physics" title="Modern physics">modern physics</a></i> arose in the early 20th century with the advent of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quantum_physics" title="Quantum physics">quantum physics</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> substituting <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_physics" title="Mathematical physics">mathematical studies</a> for <a href="/wiki/Experimental_physics" title="Experimental physics">experimental studies</a> and examining <a href="/wiki/Equation" title="Equation">equations</a> to build a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theoretical_structure" title="Theoretical structure">theoretical structure</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Characterizing modern physics as substituting theory for experiment is an incredible claim. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Old_quantum_theory" title="Old quantum theory">old quantum theory</a> was a collection of results which predate modern <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum mechanics</a>, but were never complete or self-consistent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HaarQM_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-HaarQM-40">[39]</a></sup> The collection of <a href="/wiki/Heuristic" title="Heuristic">heuristic</a> prescriptions for quantum mechanics were the first corrections to <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">classical mechanics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HaarQM_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-HaarQM-40">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> Outside the realm of quantum physics, the various <a href="/wiki/Aether_theories" title="Aether theories">aether theories</a> in classical physics, which supposed a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_elements" title="Classical elements">fifth element</a>" such as the <a href="/wiki/Luminiferous_aether" title="Luminiferous aether">Luminiferous aether</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> were nullified by the <a href="/wiki/Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment" title="Michelson–Morley experiment">Michelson–Morley experiment</a>—an attempt to detect the motion of earth through the aether. In biology, <a href="/wiki/Darwinism" title="Darwinism">Darwinism</a> gained acceptance, promoting the concept of <a href="/wiki/Adaptation" title="Adaptation">adaptation</a> in the theory of <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">natural selection</a>. The fields of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_geology" title="Modern geology">geology</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_astronomy" title="Modern astronomy">astronomy</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_psychology" title="Modern psychology">psychology</a> also made strides and gained new insights. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_medicine" title="Modern medicine">medicine</a>, there were advances in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_theory" title="Medical theory">medical theory</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_treatment" title="Medical treatment">treatments</a>.
</p><p>Starting one-hundred years before the 20th century, the <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_(spiritual)" title="Enlightenment (spiritual)">enlightenment spiritual philosophy</a> was challenged in various quarters around the 1900s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> Developed from earlier <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secular" title="Secular">secular</a> traditions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> modern <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">Humanist</a> <a href="/wiki/Ethics" title="Ethics">ethical philosophies</a> affirmed the dignity and worth of all people, based on the ability to determine right and wrong by appealing to universal human qualities, particularly <a href="/wiki/Rationalism" title="Rationalism">rationality</a>, without resorting to the supernatural or alleged divine authority from religious texts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> For <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberal_humanism" title="Liberal humanism">liberal humanists</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau" title="Jean-Jacques Rousseau">Rousseau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Kant" title="Immanuel Kant">Kant</a>, the universal law of <a href="/wiki/Reason" title="Reason">reason</a> guided the way toward total emancipation from any kind of tyranny. These ideas were challenged, for example by the <a href="/wiki/Young_Marx" title="Young Marx">young Karl Marx</a>, who criticized the project of political emancipation (embodied in the form of <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>), asserting it to be symptomatic of the very dehumanization it was supposed to oppose. For <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Nietzsche" title="Friedrich Nietzsche">Friedrich Nietzsche</a>, humanism was nothing more than a secular version of <a href="/wiki/Theism" title="Theism">theism</a>. In his <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genealogy_of_Morals" title="Genealogy of Morals">Genealogy of Morals</a></i>, he argues that human rights exist as a means for the weak to collectively constrain the strong. On this view, such rights do not facilitate emancipation of life, but rather deny it. In the 20th century, the notion that human beings are rationally autonomous was challenged by the concept that humans were driven by unconscious irrational desires.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_persons">Notable persons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Notable persons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_1921_by_F_Schmutzer.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3313" data-file-width="2523" decoding="async" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Albert_Einstein_1921_by_F_Schmutzer.jpg/170px-Albert_Einstein_1921_by_F_Schmutzer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Albert_Einstein_1921_by_F_Schmutzer.jpg/255px-Albert_Einstein_1921_by_F_Schmutzer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Albert_Einstein_1921_by_F_Schmutzer.jpg/340px-Albert_Einstein_1921_by_F_Schmutzer.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_1921_by_F_Schmutzer.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Albert Einstein in 1921</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sigmund_Freud" title="Sigmund Freud">Sigmund Freud</a> is renowned for his redefinition of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_desire" title="Sexual desire">sexual desire</a> as the primary motivational energy of human life, as well as his therapeutic techniques, including the use of <a href="/wiki/Free_association_(psychology)" title="Free association (psychology)">free association</a>, his <a href="/wiki/Transference" title="Transference">theory of transference</a> in the therapeutic relationship, and the <a href="/wiki/Dream_interpretation" title="Dream interpretation">interpretation of dreams</a> as sources of insight into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unconscious_desire" title="Unconscious desire">unconscious desires</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a> is known for his theories of <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">special relativity</a> and <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a>. He also made important contributions to <a href="/wiki/Statistical_mechanics" title="Statistical mechanics">statistical mechanics</a>, especially his mathematical treatment of <a href="/wiki/Brownian_motion" title="Brownian motion">Brownian motion</a>, his resolution of the <a href="/wiki/Einstein_solid" title="Einstein solid">paradox of specific heats</a>, and his connection of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fluctuation_dissipation_theorem" title="Fluctuation dissipation theorem">fluctuations and dissipation</a>. Despite his reservations about its interpretation, Einstein also made contributions to quantum mechanics and, indirectly, <a href="/wiki/Quantum_field_theory" title="Quantum field theory">quantum field theory</a>, primarily through his theoretical studies of the <a href="/wiki/Photon" title="Photon">photon</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_Darwinism">Social Darwinism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Social Darwinism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the end of the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Social_Darwinism" title="Social Darwinism">Social Darwinism</a> was promoted and included the various ideologies based on a concept that competition among all individuals, groups, nations, or ideas was a "natural" framework for social evolution in human societies. In this view, society's advancement is dependent on the "<a href="/wiki/Survival_of_the_fittest" title="Survival of the fittest">survival of the fittest</a>". The term was in fact coined by <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Spencer" title="Herbert Spencer">Herbert Spencer</a> and referred to in "<a href="/wiki/The_Gospel_of_Wealth" title="The Gospel of Wealth">The Gospel of Wealth</a>" written by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marxist_society">Marxist society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Marxist society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pyramid_of_Capitalist_System.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="990" data-file-width="763" decoding="async" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Pyramid_of_Capitalist_System.jpg/220px-Pyramid_of_Capitalist_System.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Pyramid_of_Capitalist_System.jpg/330px-Pyramid_of_Capitalist_System.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Pyramid_of_Capitalist_System.jpg/440px-Pyramid_of_Capitalist_System.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pyramid_of_Capitalist_System.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1911 <i>Industrial Worker</i> (<a href="/wiki/Industrial_Workers_of_the_World" title="Industrial Workers of the World">IWW</a> newspaper) publication advocating industrial unionism that shows a critique of capitalism.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Karl Marx</a> summarized his approach to history and politics in the opening line of the first chapter of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Communist_Manifesto" title="The Communist Manifesto">The Communist Manifesto</a></i> (1848). He wrote:
</p>
<dl><dd><i>The history of all hitherto existing society is the history of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_struggle" title="Class struggle">class struggles</a>.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>The <i>Manifesto</i> went through a number of editions from 1872 to 1890; notable new prefaces were written by Marx and Engels for the 1872 German edition, the 1882 Russian edition, the 1883 German edition, and the 1888 English edition. In general, <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> identified five (and one transitional) successive stages of development in Western Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primitive_Communism" title="Primitive Communism">Primitive Communism</a>: as seen in cooperative tribal societies.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave" title="Slave">Slave</a> Society: which develops when the tribe becomes a city-state. Aristocracy is born.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">Feudalism</a>: aristocracy is the ruling class. Merchants develop into capitalists.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">Capitalism</a>: capitalists are the ruling class, who create and employ the true working class.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dictatorship_of_the_proletariat" title="Dictatorship of the proletariat">Dictatorship of the proletariat</a>: workers gain class consciousness, <a href="/wiki/Proletarian_revolution" title="Proletarian revolution">overthrow</a> the capitalists and take control over the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">state</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Communism</a>: a <a href="/wiki/Classless_society" title="Classless society">classless</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stateless_society" title="Stateless society">stateless society</a>.</li></ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_decline_and_the_20th_century">European decline and the 20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: European decline and the 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/20th_century" title="20th century">20th century</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Australia_1900.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1276" data-file-width="1699" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Australia_1900.jpg/220px-Australia_1900.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Australia_1900.jpg/330px-Australia_1900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Australia_1900.jpg/440px-Australia_1900.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Australia_1900.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Though still tied to <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Great Britain</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">commonwealth</a> <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> achieved peaceful independence in 1901.</div></div></div>
<p>Major political developments saw the former <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> lose most of its remaining political power over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Commonwealth" title="British Commonwealth">commonwealth</a> countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian Railway</a>, crossing Asia by train, was complete by 1916. Other events include the <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli–Palestinian conflict">Israeli–Palestinian conflict</a>, two world wars, and the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australian_Constitution">Australian Constitution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Australian Constitution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1901, the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Australia" title="Federation of Australia">Federation of Australia</a> was the process by which the six separate British <a href="/wiki/Self-governing_colony" title="Self-governing colony">self-governing colonies</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a> formed one nation. They kept the systems of government that they had developed as separate colonies but also would have a federal government that was responsible for matters concerning the whole nation. When the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Australia" title="Constitution of Australia">Constitution of Australia</a> came into force, the colonies collectively became <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">states</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Commonwealth of Australia</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolution_and_Warlords_in_China">Revolution and Warlords in China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Revolution and Warlords in China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="639" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg/220px-Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg/330px-Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg/440px-Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a> in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>; <a href="/wiki/Chen_Qimei" title="Chen Qimei">Chen Qimei</a> organized Shanghainese civilians to start the uprising and was successful. The picture above is <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Road" title="Nanjing Road">Nanjing Road</a> after the uprising, hung with the <a href="/wiki/Five_Races_Under_One_Union" title="Five Races Under One Union">Five Races Under One Union</a> Flags then used by the revolutionaries.</div></div></div>
<p>The last days of the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a> were marked with civil unrest, <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Days%27_Reform" title="Hundred Days' Reform">failed reforms</a> and foreign invasions such as the <a href="/wiki/Boxer_Rebellion" title="Boxer Rebellion">Boxer rebellion</a>. Responding to these civil failures and discontent, the Qing Imperial Court did attempt to reform the government in various ways, as the decision to draft a constitution in 1906, the establishment of provincial legislatures in 1909, and the preparation for a national parliament in 1910. However, many of these measures were opposed by the conservatives of the Qing Court, and many reformers were either imprisoned or executed outright. The failures of the Imperial Court to enact such reforming measures of political liberalization and modernization caused the reformists to steer toward the road of revolution.
</p><p>The assertions of Chinese philosophy<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> began to integrate concepts of Western philosophy, as steps toward modernization. By the time of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a> in 1911, there were many calls, such as the <a href="/wiki/May_Fourth_Movement" title="May Fourth Movement">May Fourth Movement</a>, to completely abolish the old imperial institutions and practices of China. There were attempts to incorporate <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">republicanism</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrialism" title="Industrialism">industrialism</a> into Chinese philosophy, notably by <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a> at the beginning of the 20th century
</p><p>In 1912, the Republic of China was established and Sun Yat-sen was inaugurated in <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a> as the first <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="President of the Republic of China">Provisional President</a>. But power in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> already had passed to <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Shikai" title="Yuan Shikai">Yuan Shikai</a>, who had effective control of the <a href="/wiki/Beiyang_Army" title="Beiyang Army">Beiyang Army</a>, the most powerful military force in China at the time. To prevent <a href="/wiki/Civil_war" title="Civil war">civil war</a> and possible foreign intervention from undermining the infant republic, leaders agreed to Army's demand that China be united under a Beijing government. On March 10, in Beijing, Shikai was sworn in as the second Provisional President of the Republic of China.
</p><p>After the early 20th century revolutions, shifting alliances of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warlord_era_(China)" title="Warlord era (China)">China's regional warlords</a> waged war for control of the Beijing government. Despite the fact that various warlords gained control of the government in Beijing during the warlord era, this did not constitute a new era of control or governance, because other warlords did not acknowledge the transitory governments in this period and were a law unto themselves. These military-dominated governments were collectively known as the <a href="/wiki/Beiyang_government" title="Beiyang government">Beiyang government</a>. The warlord era ended around 1927.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Start_of_the_20th_century">Start of the 20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Start of the 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="624" data-file-width="1560" decoding="async" height="280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png/700px-World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png/1050px-World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png/1400px-World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png 2x" width="700"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The World in 1898 color coded for major empires. The <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing Dynasty</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> were the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires" title="List of largest empires">largest countries</a> at the time.</div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Yalu_River_1904.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1299" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Battle_of_Yalu_River_1904.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Yalu_River_1904.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Battle_of_Yalu_River_1904.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Yalu_River_1904.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Battle_of_Yalu_River_1904.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Yalu_River_1904.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Yalu_River_1904.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a> was the first time a European country was defeated by an Asian country in modern times. The Japanese victory shocked the world.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1900 the World's Population had approached approximately 1.6 billion.
Four years into the 20th century saw the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Port_Arthur" title="Battle of Port Arthur">Battle of Port Arthur</a> establishing the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> as a world power. The Russians were in constant pursuit of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warm_water_port" title="Warm water port">warm water port</a> on the Pacific Ocean, for their navy as well as for maritime trade. The Manchurian Campaign of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> was fought against the Japanese over <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>. The major theatres of operations were Southern Manchuria, specifically the area around the <a href="/wiki/Liaodong_Peninsula" title="Liaodong Peninsula">Liaodong Peninsula</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mukden" title="Mukden">Mukden</a>, and the seas around Korea, Japan, and the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Sea" title="Yellow Sea">Yellow Sea</a>. The resulting campaigns, in which the fledgling Japanese military consistently attained victory over the Russian forces arrayed against them, were unexpected by world observers. These victories, as time transpired, would dramatically transform the distribution of power in East Asia, resulting in a reassessment of Japan's recent entry onto the world stage. The embarrassing string of defeats increased Russian popular dissatisfaction with the inefficient and corrupt Tsarist government.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_of_1905" title="Russian Revolution of 1905">Russian Revolution of 1905</a> was a wave of mass political unrest through vast areas of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>. Some of it was directed against the government, while some was undirected.  It included <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a>, worker strikes, peasant unrests, and military mutinies. It led to the establishment of the limited constitutional monarchy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> the establishment of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Duma_of_the_Russian_Empire" title="State Duma of the Russian Empire">State Duma of the Russian Empire</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>.
</p><p>In China, the Qing Dynasty was overthrown following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a>. The Xinhai Revolution began with the <a href="/wiki/Wuchang_Uprising" title="Wuchang Uprising">Wuchang Uprising</a> on October 10, 1911, and ended with the abdication of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emperor_Puyi" title="Emperor Puyi">Emperor Puyi</a> on February 12, 1912. The primary parties to the conflict were the Imperial forces of the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a> (1644–1911), and the revolutionary forces of the <a href="/wiki/Tongmenghui" title="Tongmenghui">Chinese Revolutionary Alliance</a> (Tongmenghui).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Edwardian_Britain">Edwardian Britain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Edwardian Britain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Titanic_in_color.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3016" data-file-width="4100" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Titanic_in_color.png/220px-Titanic_in_color.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Titanic_in_color.png/330px-Titanic_in_color.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Titanic_in_color.png/440px-Titanic_in_color.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Titanic_in_color.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic" title="Titanic">Titanic</a></i> was the largest ship constructed in her time. Deemed invincible, she was <a href="/wiki/Sinking_of_the_Titanic" title="Sinking of the Titanic">sunk</a> by <a href="/wiki/Iceberg" title="Iceberg">icebergs</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Labrador" title="Labrador">Labrador, Canada.</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Edwardian_era" title="Edwardian era">Edwardian era</a> in the United Kingdom is the period spanning the reign of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_VII_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Edward VII of the United Kingdom">King Edward VII</a> up to the end of the First World War, including the years surrounding the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinking_of_the_RMS_Titanic" title="Sinking of the RMS Titanic">sinking of the RMS <i>Titanic</i></a>. In the early years of the period, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Second Boer War</a> in South Africa split the country into anti- and pro-war factions. The imperial policies of the Conservatives eventually proved unpopular and in the <a href="/wiki/1906_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1906 United Kingdom general election">general election of 1906</a> the Liberals won a huge landslide. The Liberal government was unable to proceed with all of its radical programme without the support of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>, which was largely Conservative. Conflict between the two Houses of Parliament over the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Budget" title="People's Budget">People's Budget</a> led to a reduction in the power of the peers in 1910. The <a href="/wiki/January_1910_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="January 1910 United Kingdom general election">general election in January that year</a> returned a <a href="/wiki/Hung_parliament" title="Hung parliament">hung parliament</a> with the balance of power held by <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Party_(Ireland)" title="Nationalist Party (Ireland)">Irish Nationalist</a> members.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: World War I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Causes_of_World_War_I" title="Causes of World War I">causes of World War I</a> included many factors, including the conflicts and antagonisms of the four decades leading up to the war. The <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a> was the name given to the loose alignment between the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a> after the signing of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Russian_Entente" title="Anglo-Russian Entente">Anglo-Russian Entente</a> in 1907.  The alignment of the three powers, supplemented by various agreements with <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japan</a>, the United States, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spain_under_the_Restoration" title="Spain under the Restoration">Spain</a>, constituted a powerful counterweight to the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Alliance_(1882)" title="Triple Alliance (1882)">Triple Alliance</a> of <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Italy</a>, the third having concluded an additional secret agreement with France effectively nullifying her Alliance commitments. Militarism, alliances, imperialism, and nationalism played major roles in the conflict. The immediate origins of the war lay in the decisions taken by statesmen and generals during the <a href="/wiki/July_Crisis" title="July Crisis">July Crisis</a> of 1914, the spark (or casus belli) for which was the assassination of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand" title="Archduke Franz Ferdinand">Archduke Franz Ferdinand</a> of Austria.
</p><p>However, the crisis did not exist in a void; it came after a long series of diplomatic clashes between the Great Powers over European and colonial issues in the decade prior to 1914 which had left tensions high. The diplomatic clashes can be traced to changes in the balance of power in Europe since 1870.
