An example is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baghdad_Railway" title="Baghdad Railway">Baghdad Railway</a> which was planned to connect the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> cities of <a href="/wiki/Konya" title="Konya">Konya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> with a line through modern-day Turkey, Syria and Iraq. The railway became a source of international disputes during the years immediately preceding World War I. Although it has been argued that they were resolved in 1914 before the war began, it has also been argued that the railroad was a cause of the First World War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> Fundamentally the war was sparked by tensions over territory in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>. Austria-Hungary competed with Serbia and Russia for territory and influence in the region and they pulled the rest of the great powers into the conflict through their various alliances and treaties. The <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a> were two wars in South-eastern Europe in 1912–1913 in the course of which the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_League" title="Balkan League">Balkan League</a> (Bulgaria, Montenegro, Greece, and Serbia) first captured Ottoman-held remaining part of Thessaly, Macedonia, Epirus, Albania and most of Thrace and then fell out over the division of the spoils, with incorporation of Romania this time.
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World_War_1.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" decoding="async" height="347" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/World_War_1.gif/750px-World_War_1.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/World_War_1.gif/1125px-World_War_1.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e4/World_War_1.gif 2x" width="750"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World_War_1.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Various periods of World War I; 1914.07.28 (Tsar Nicholas II of Russia orders a partial mobilization against Austria-Hungary), 1914.08.01 (Germany declares war on Russia), 1914.08.03 (Germany declares war on Russia's ally France), 1914.08.04 (Britain declares war on Germany), 1914.12 (British and German <a href="/wiki/Christmas_truce" title="Christmas truce">Christmas truce</a>), 1915.12 (French and German Christmas truce), 1916.12 (<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Magdhaba" title="Battle of Magdhaba">Battle of Magdhaba</a>), 1917.12 (British troops take Jerusalem from the Ottoman Empire), and 1918.11.11 (World War I ends: Germany signs an armistice agreement with the Allies). Allies and Central Powers in the First World War<br/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#088A08; color:black;"> </span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#01DF01; color:black;"> </span> Allied powers and areas<br/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FE9A2E; color:black;"> </span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#F7BE81; color:black;"> </span> Central powers and colonies or occupied territory<br/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#BDBDBD; color:black;"> </span> Neutral countries</div></div></div></div>
<p>The First World War began in 1914 and lasted to the final <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armistice_with_Germany_(Compi%C3%A8gne)" title="Armistice with Germany (Compiègne)">Armistice</a> in 1918. The <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied Powers</a>, led by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Britain_in_World_War_I" title="Britain in World War I">British Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a>, Russia until March 1918, Japan and the United States after 1917, defeated the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a>, led by the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. The war caused the disintegration of four empires—the Austro-Hungarian, German, Ottoman, and Russian ones—as well as radical change in the European and West Asian maps. The Allied powers before 1917 are referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a>, and the Central Powers are referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Alliance_(1882)" title="Triple Alliance (1882)">Triple Alliance</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chemical_Warfare_in_the_Twentieth_Century_Q54781.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="583" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Chemical_Warfare_in_the_Twentieth_Century_Q54781.jpg/220px-Chemical_Warfare_in_the_Twentieth_Century_Q54781.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Chemical_Warfare_in_the_Twentieth_Century_Q54781.jpg/330px-Chemical_Warfare_in_the_Twentieth_Century_Q54781.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Chemical_Warfare_in_the_Twentieth_Century_Q54781.jpg/440px-Chemical_Warfare_in_the_Twentieth_Century_Q54781.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chemical_Warfare_in_the_Twentieth_Century_Q54781.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Italian <i><a href="/wiki/Arditi" title="Arditi">Arditi</a></i> troops using <a href="/wiki/Gas_mask" title="Gas mask">gas-masks</a> to protect themselves from <a href="/wiki/Chemical_warfare" title="Chemical warfare">Chemical Warfare</a>, used for the first time in WWI.</div></div></div><p>Much of the fighting in World War I took place along the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a>, within a system of opposing manned trenches and fortifications (separated by a "<a href="/wiki/No_man%27s_land" title="No man's land">No man's land</a>") running from the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> to the border of Switzerland. On the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Eastern Front (World War I)">Eastern Front</a>, the vast eastern plains and limited rail network prevented a trench warfare stalemate from developing, although the scale of the conflict was just as large.  Hostilities also occurred on and under the sea and—for the first time—from the air. More than 9 million soldiers died on the various battlefields, and nearly that many more in the participating countries' home fronts on account of food shortages and <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> committed under the cover of various civil wars and internal conflicts. Notably, more people died of the worldwide <a href="/wiki/Spanish_flu" title="Spanish flu">influenza outbreak</a> at the end of the war and shortly after than died in the hostilities. The unsanitary conditions engendered by the war, severe overcrowding in barracks, wartime propaganda interfering with public health warnings, and migration of so many soldiers around the world helped the outbreak become a <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">pandemic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ultimately, World War I created a decisive break with the old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_World_Order_(political)" title="New World Order (political)">world order</a> that had emerged after the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, which was modified by the mid-19th century's nationalistic revolutions. The results of World War I would be important factors in the development of World War II approximately 20 years later. More immediate to the time, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Partitioning_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Partitioning of the Ottoman Empire">partitioning of the Ottoman Empire</a> was a political event that redrew the political boundaries of West Asia. The huge conglomeration of territories and peoples formerly ruled by the Sultan of the Ottoman Empire was divided into several new nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> The partitioning brought the creation of the modern <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Turkey" title="Republic of Turkey">Republic of Turkey</a>. The <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> granted France mandates over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Mandate_of_Syria" title="French Mandate of Syria">Syria</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Mandate_of_Lebanon" title="French Mandate of Lebanon">Lebanon</a> and granted the United Kingdom mandates over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Mandate_of_Mesopotamia" title="British Mandate of Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mandate_for_Palestine" title="Mandate for Palestine">Palestine</a> (which was later divided into two regions: <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Palestine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">Transjordan</a>). Parts of the Ottoman Empire on the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a> became parts of what are today <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolution_and_war_in_Russia">Revolution and war in Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Revolution and war in Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lenin.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="120" data-file-width="160" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f1/Lenin.gif" width="160"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lenin.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lenin</div></div></div>
<p>The Russian Revolution is the series of revolutions in Russia in 1917, which destroyed the <a href="/wiki/Tsarist_autocracy" title="Tsarist autocracy">Tsarist autocracy</a> and led to the creation of the Soviet Union. Following the abdication of <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">Nicholas II of Russia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government" title="Russian Provisional Government">Russian Provisional Government</a> was established. In October 1917, a <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution"><i>red</i> faction revolution</a> occurred in which the <a href="/wiki/Red_Guards_(Russia)" title="Red Guards (Russia)">Red Guard</a>, armed groups of workers and deserting soldiers directed by the Bolshevik Party, seized control of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> (then known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrograd" title="Petrograd">Petrograd</a>) and began an immediate armed takeover of cities and villages throughout the former <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>.
</p><p>Another action in 1917 that is of note was the armistice signed between Russia and the Central Powers at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brest-Litovsk" title="Brest-Litovsk">Brest-Litovsk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> As a condition for peace, the treaty by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> conceded huge portions of the former Russian Empire to <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Imperial Germany</a> and the Ottoman Empire, greatly upsetting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationalist" title="Nationalist">nationalists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">conservatives</a>. The Bolsheviks made peace with the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a>, as they had promised the Russian people prior to the Revolution. Vladimir Lenin's decision has been attributed to his sponsorship by the foreign office of <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_II,_German_Emperor" title="Wilhelm II, German Emperor">Wilhelm II, German Emperor</a>, offered by the latter in hopes that with a revolution, Russia would withdraw from World War I. This suspicion was bolstered by the German Foreign Ministry's sponsorship of Lenin's return to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Petrograd</a>.  The <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Western Allies</a> expressed their dismay at the Bolsheviks, upset at:
</p>
<ol><li>the withdrawal of Russia from the war effort,</li>
<li>worried about a possible Russo-German alliance, and</li>
<li>galvanized by the prospect of the Bolsheviks making good their threats to assume no responsibility for, and so default on, Imperial Russia's massive <a href="/wiki/External_debt" title="External debt">foreign loans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup></li></ol>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russian_civil_war_posters.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Russian_civil_war_posters.png/220px-Russian_civil_war_posters.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Russian_civil_war_posters.png/330px-Russian_civil_war_posters.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Russian_civil_war_posters.png/440px-Russian_civil_war_posters.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russian_civil_war_posters.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two contrasting visions of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>. To the left is propaganda from the <a href="/wiki/White_Army" title="White Army">White Army</a>, to the right is propaganda from the <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">Bolsheviks</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In addition, there was a concern, shared by many <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> as well, that the socialist revolutionary ideas would spread to the West. Hence, many of these countries expressed their support for the Whites, including the provision of troops and supplies. <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> declared that Bolshevism must be "strangled in its cradle".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Russian Civil War was a multi-party war that occurred within the former <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_provisional_government" title="Russian provisional government">Russian provisional government</a> collapsed and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_republic_(system_of_government)" title="Soviet republic (system of government)">Soviets</a> under the domination of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshevik" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> party assumed power, first in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Petrograd (St. Petersburg)</a> and then in other places. In the wake of the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a>, the old Russian Imperial Army had been demobilized; the volunteer-based Red Guard was the Bolsheviks' main military force, augmented by an armed military component of the <a href="/wiki/Cheka" title="Cheka">Cheka</a>, the Bolshevik state security apparatus. There was an instituted mandatory conscription of the rural peasantry into the Red Army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> Opposition of rural Russians to Red Army conscription units was overcome by taking hostages and shooting them when necessary in order to force compliance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> Former Tsarist officers were utilized as "military specialists" (<i>voenspetsy</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> taking their families hostage in order to ensure loyalty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams,_Beryl_1921_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Williams,_Beryl_1921-67">[66]</a></sup> At the start of the war, three-fourths of the Red Army officer corps was composed of former Tsarist officers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams,_Beryl_1921_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-Williams,_Beryl_1921-67">[66]</a></sup> By its end, 83% of all Red Army divisional and corps commanders were ex-Tsarist soldiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vladivostok_intervention.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="588" data-file-width="841" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Vladivostok_intervention.jpg/220px-Vladivostok_intervention.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Vladivostok_intervention.jpg/330px-Vladivostok_intervention.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Vladivostok_intervention.jpg/440px-Vladivostok_intervention.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vladivostok_intervention.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In the Russian Civil War, over eleven nations intervened in favor of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Movement" title="White Movement">White Movement</a>. Here Japanese occupy <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The principal fighting occurred between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshevik" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> and the forces of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Movement" title="White Movement">White Army</a>. Many foreign armies warred against the Red Army, notably the <a href="/wiki/Allied_intervention_in_the_Russian_Civil_War" title="Allied intervention in the Russian Civil War">Allied Forces</a>, yet many volunteer foreigners fought in both sides of the Russian Civil War. Other nationalist and regional political groups also participated in the war, including the Ukrainian nationalist <a href="/wiki/Green_armies" title="Green armies">Green Army</a>, the Ukrainian anarchist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Insurrectionary_Army_of_Ukraine" title="Revolutionary Insurrectionary Army of Ukraine">Black Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_Guards" title="Black Guards">Black Guards</a>, and warlords such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ungern_von_Sternberg" title="Ungern von Sternberg">Ungern von Sternberg</a>. The most intense fighting took place from 1918 to 1920. Major military operations ended on 25 October 1922 when the Red Army occupied <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a>, previously held by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Provisional_Priamur_Government" title="Provisional Priamur Government">Provisional Priamur Government</a>. The last enclave of the White Forces was the <a href="/wiki/Ayano-Maysky_District" title="Ayano-Maysky District">Ayano-Maysky District</a> on the Pacific coast. The majority of the fighting ended in 1920 with the defeat of General <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Wrangel" title="Pyotr Wrangel">Pyotr Wrangel</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a>, but a notable resistance in certain areas continued until 1923 (e.g., <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kronstadt_Uprising" title="Kronstadt Uprising">Kronstadt Uprising</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tambov_Rebellion" title="Tambov Rebellion">Tambov Rebellion</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basmachi_Revolt" title="Basmachi Revolt">Basmachi Revolt</a>, and the final resistance of the <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">White movement</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">Far East</a>).
</p><p>While the early 1920s was a time of flux for revolutionary Russia and Central Asia, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_of_Soviet_Socialist_Republics" title="Union of Soviet Socialist Republics">Union of Soviet Socialist Republics</a> was proclaimed in 1922 as the successor state to the fallen <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>. Revolutionary leader <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> died of natural causes and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Early_Republic_of_China">The Early Republic of China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: The Early Republic of China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1917, China declared war on Germany in the hope of recovering its lost province, then under Japanese control. The <a href="/wiki/New_Culture_Movement" title="New Culture Movement">New Culture Movement</a> occupied the period from 1917 to 1923. Chinese representatives refused to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>, due to intense pressure from the student protesters and public opinion alike.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Student_Demonstrations,_June_4th_and_5th,_1919_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="881" data-file-width="1117" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Student_Demonstrations%2C_June_4th_and_5th%2C_1919_2.jpg/220px-Student_Demonstrations%2C_June_4th_and_5th%2C_1919_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Student_Demonstrations%2C_June_4th_and_5th%2C_1919_2.jpg/330px-Student_Demonstrations%2C_June_4th_and_5th%2C_1919_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Student_Demonstrations%2C_June_4th_and_5th%2C_1919_2.jpg/440px-Student_Demonstrations%2C_June_4th_and_5th%2C_1919_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Student_Demonstrations,_June_4th_and_5th,_1919_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Student Demonstrations on 3 June 1919</div></div></div><p>
The <a href="/wiki/May_Fourth_Movement" title="May Fourth Movement">May Fourth Movement</a> helped to rekindle the then-fading cause of republican revolution. In 1917 <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a> had become commander-in-chief of a rival military government in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a> in collaboration with southern warlords. Sun's efforts to obtain aid from the Western democracies were ignored, however, and in 1920 he turned to the Soviet Union, which had recently achieved its own revolution. The Soviets sought to befriend the Chinese revolutionists by offering scathing attacks on Western imperialism. But for political expediency, the Soviet leadership initiated a dual policy of support for both Sun and the newly established <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chinese Communist Party">Chinese Communist Party</a> (CCP).</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sino-german_cooperation.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="553" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sino-german_cooperation.png/150px-Sino-german_cooperation.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sino-german_cooperation.png/225px-Sino-german_cooperation.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sino-german_cooperation.png/300px-Sino-german_cooperation.png 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sino-german_cooperation.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>With <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sino-German_cooperation_until_1941" title="Sino-German cooperation until 1941">Sino-German cooperation until 1941</a>, Chinese industry and military was improved just prior to the war against Japan.</div></div></div>
<p>In early 1927, the Kuomintang-CCP rivalry led to a split in the revolutionary ranks. The CCP and the left wing of the Kuomintang had decided to move the seat of the Nationalist government from Guangzhou to <a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">Wuhan</a>. But <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>, whose <a href="/wiki/Northern_Expedition" title="Northern Expedition">Northern Expedition</a> was proving successful, set his forces to destroying the Shanghai CCP apparatus and established an anti-Communist government at Nanjing in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/April_12_Incident" title="April 12 Incident">April 1927</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nanjing_period_in_China">Nanjing period in China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Nanjing period in China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_decade" title="Nanjing decade">Nanjing decade</a></div>
<p>The "Nanjing Decade" of 1928–37 was one of consolidation and accomplishment under the leadership of the Nationalists, with a mixed but generally positive record in the economy, social progress, development of <a href="/wiki/Democracy_in_China" title="Democracy in China">democracy</a>, and cultural creativity. Some of the harsh aspects of foreign concessions and privileges in China were moderated through diplomacy.
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sino-German_cooperation_(1926%E2%80%931941)" title="Sino-German cooperation (1926–1941)">Sino-German cooperation (1926–1941)</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Resources_Commission" title="National Resources Commission">National Resources Commission</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_1920s_and_the_Depression">The 1920s and the Depression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: The 1920s and the Depression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">Interwar period</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roaring_Twenties" title="Roaring Twenties">Roaring Twenties</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a></div>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World_1920_empires_colonies_territory.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="634" data-file-width="1616" decoding="async" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/World_1920_empires_colonies_territory.png/700px-World_1920_empires_colonies_territory.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/World_1920_empires_colonies_territory.png/1050px-World_1920_empires_colonies_territory.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/World_1920_empires_colonies_territory.png/1400px-World_1920_empires_colonies_territory.png 2x" width="700"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World_1920_empires_colonies_territory.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The world in 1920, part of the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar period</a>. <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Great Britain</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> expanded greatly at the expense of the former <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>The interwar period was the period between the end of the First World War and the beginning of the Second World War. This period was marked by turmoil in much of the world, as Europe struggled to recover from the devastation of the First World War.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_flapper_girl_LCCN2012645724.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="1017" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/A_flapper_girl_LCCN2012645724.tif/lossy-page1-150px-A_flapper_girl_LCCN2012645724.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/A_flapper_girl_LCCN2012645724.tif/lossy-page1-226px-A_flapper_girl_LCCN2012645724.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/A_flapper_girl_LCCN2012645724.tif/lossy-page1-300px-A_flapper_girl_LCCN2012645724.tif.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_flapper_girl_LCCN2012645724.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>American, Flapper Girl. In the 1920s women experienced a degree of <a href="/wiki/First-wave_feminism" title="First-wave feminism">liberation</a>.</div></div></div><p>
In North America, especially the first half of this period, people experienced considerable prosperity in the Roaring Twenties. The social and societal upheaval known as the Roaring Twenties began in North America and spread to Europe in the <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I" title="Aftermath of World War I">aftermath of World War I</a>. The <i>Roaring Twenties</i>, often called "<a href="/wiki/Jazz_Age" title="Jazz Age">The Jazz Age</a>", saw an exposition of social, artistic, and cultural dynamism. "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Normalcy" title="Normalcy">Normalcy</a>" returned to politics, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jazz_music" title="Jazz music">jazz music</a> blossomed, the <a href="/wiki/Flapper" title="Flapper">flapper</a> redefined modern womanhood, <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> peaked. The spirit of the Roaring Twenties was marked by a general feeling of discontinuity associated with modernity, a break with traditions. Everything seemed to be feasible through modern technology. New technologies, especially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">automobiles</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movies" title="Movies">movies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radio" title="Radio">radio</a> proliferated "modernity" to a large part of the population. The 1920s saw the general favor of practicality, in architecture as well as in daily life. The 1920s was further distinguished by several inventions and discoveries, extensive industrial growth and the rise in consumer demand and aspirations, and significant changes in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lifestyle_(sociology)" title="Lifestyle (sociology)">lifestyle</a>.</p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><audio class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="256" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="I_Got_The_Ritz_From_The_One_I_Love.ogg" id="mwe_player_3" preload="none" style="width:220px;" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="105908" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (106 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4a/I_Got_The_Ritz_From_The_One_I_Love.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="149472" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/4a/I_Got_The_Ritz_From_The_One_I_Love.ogg/I_Got_The_Ritz_From_The_One_I_Love.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/></audio> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:I_Got_The_Ritz_From_The_One_I_Love.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>I got the Ritz from the one I love,</i> Jazz music radio broadcast 1932</div></div></div><p>
Europe spent these years rebuilding and coming to terms with the vast human cost of the conflict. The <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Istanbul" title="Occupation of Istanbul">occupation of Istanbul</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Izmir" title="Izmir">Izmir</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> by the Allies in the aftermath of World War I prompted the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_National_Movement" title="Turkish National Movement">Turkish National Movement</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence" title="Turkish War of Independence">Turkish War of Independence</a> (1919–1923) was waged with the aim of revoking the terms of the Treaty of Sèvres. After the Turkish victory, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lausanne" title="Treaty of Lausanne">Treaty of Lausanne</a> of 24 July 1923 led to the international recognition of the sovereignty of the newly formed "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Turkey" title="Republic of Turkey">Republic of Turkey</a>" as the successor state of the Ottoman Empire, and the republic was officially proclaimed on 29 October 1923 in Ankara, the country's new capital. The Lausanne Convention stipulated a <a href="/wiki/Population_exchange_between_Greece_and_Turkey" title="Population exchange between Greece and Turkey">population exchange between Greece and Turkey</a>, whereby 1.1 million Greeks left Turkey for Greece in exchange for 380,000 Muslims transferred from Greece to Turkey. The economy of the United States became increasingly intertwined with that of Europe. In Germany, the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a> gave way to episodes of political and economic turmoil, which culminated with the <a href="/wiki/Hyperinflation_in_the_Weimar_Republic" title="Hyperinflation in the Weimar Republic">German hyperinflation</a> of 1923 and the failed <a href="/wiki/Beer_Hall_Putsch" title="Beer Hall Putsch">Beer Hall Putsch</a> of that same year. When Germany could no longer afford war payments, Wall Street invested heavily in European debts to keep the European economy afloat as a large consumer market for American mass-produced goods. By the middle of the decade, <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a> soared in Europe, and the Roaring Twenties broke out in Germany, Britain and France, the second half of the decade becoming known as the "<a href="/wiki/Golden_Twenties" title="Golden Twenties">Golden Twenties</a>". In France and francophone Canada, they were also called the "<i>années folles</i>" ("Crazy Years"). </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Depression,_Breadlines-long_line_of_people_waiting_to_be_fed,_New_York_City,_in_the_absence_of_substantial_government..._-_NARA_-_196506.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1608" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Depression%2C_Breadlines-long_line_of_people_waiting_to_be_fed%2C_New_York_City%2C_in_the_absence_of_substantial_government..._-_NARA_-_196506.tif/lossy-page1-150px-Depression%2C_Breadlines-long_line_of_people_waiting_to_be_fed%2C_New_York_City%2C_in_the_absence_of_substantial_government..._-_NARA_-_196506.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Depression%2C_Breadlines-long_line_of_people_waiting_to_be_fed%2C_New_York_City%2C_in_the_absence_of_substantial_government..._-_NARA_-_196506.tif/lossy-page1-225px-Depression%2C_Breadlines-long_line_of_people_waiting_to_be_fed%2C_New_York_City%2C_in_the_absence_of_substantial_government..._-_NARA_-_196506.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Depression%2C_Breadlines-long_line_of_people_waiting_to_be_fed%2C_New_York_City%2C_in_the_absence_of_substantial_government..._-_NARA_-_196506.tif/lossy-page1-300px-Depression%2C_Breadlines-long_line_of_people_waiting_to_be_fed%2C_New_York_City%2C_in_the_absence_of_substantial_government..._-_NARA_-_196506.tif.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Depression,_Breadlines-long_line_of_people_waiting_to_be_fed,_New_York_City,_in_the_absence_of_substantial_government..._-_NARA_-_196506.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, Breadlines-long line of people waiting to be fed, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> i</div></div></div><p>Worldwide prosperity changed dramatically with the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> in 1929. The <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">Wall Street Crash of 1929</a> served to punctuate the end of the previous era, as <i>The Great Depression</i> set in. The <i>Great Depression</i> was a worldwide economic <a href="/wiki/Recession" title="Recession">downturn</a> starting in most places in 1929 and ending at different times in the 1930s or early 1940s for different countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CRomer1_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-CRomer1-69">[68]</a></sup> It was the largest and most important <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Depression_(economics)" title="Depression (economics)">economic depression</a> in the 20th century, and is used in the 21st century as an example of how far the world's economy can fall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>The depression had devastating effects in virtually every country, rich or poor. International trade plunged by half to two-thirds, as did personal income, tax revenue, prices and profits. <a href="/wiki/Cities_in_the_Great_Depression" title="Cities in the Great Depression">Cities all around the world</a> were hit hard, especially those dependent on <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">heavy industry</a>. Construction was virtually halted in many countries. Farming and rural areas suffered as crop prices fell by roughly 60 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USBLS_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-USBLS-71">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> Facing plummeting demand with few alternate sources of jobs, areas dependent on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_sector_of_economic_activity" title="Primary sector of economic activity">primary sector industries</a> suffered the most.
The Great Depression ended at different times in different countries with the <a href="/wiki/Home_front_during_World_War_II" title="Home front during World War II">effect lasting into the next era</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> America's Great Depression ended in 1941 with America's entry into World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> The majority of countries set up relief programs, and most underwent some sort of political upheaval, pushing them to the left or right. In some world states, the desperate citizens turned toward nationalist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demagogy" title="Demagogy">demagogues</a>—the most infamous being <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>—setting the stage for the next era of war. The convulsion brought on by the worldwide depression resulted in the rise of <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a>. In Asia, Japan became an ever more assertive power, especially with regards to China.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_League_and_crises">The League and crises</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: The League and crises">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><audio class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="69" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Another_talk_with_the_German_Chancellor,_Herr_Hitler.ogg" id="mwe_player_4" preload="none" style="width:220px;" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="57062" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (57 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a1/Another_talk_with_the_German_Chancellor%2C_Herr_Hitler.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="82696" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/a/a1/Another_talk_with_the_German_Chancellor%2C_Herr_Hitler.ogg/Another_talk_with_the_German_Chancellor%2C_Herr_Hitler.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/><track data-dir="ltr" kind="subtitles" label="English ‪(en)‬" src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3AAnother_talk_with_the_German_Chancellor%2C_Herr_Hitler.ogg&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt&amp;origin=%2A" srclang="en" type="text/vtt"/></audio> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Another_talk_with_the_German_Chancellor,_Herr_Hitler.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.K Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain" title="Neville Chamberlain">Nevil Chamberline</a> attempted to negotiate with <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> as Nazi Germany practiced an expansionist policy.</div></div></div>
<p>The interwar period was also marked by a radical change in the international order, away from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balance_of_power_in_international_relations" title="Balance of power in international relations">balance of power</a> that had dominated pre–World War I Europe. One main institution that was meant to bring stability was the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>, which was created after the First World War with the intention of maintaining world security and peace and encouraging economic growth between member countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p>
However the League failed to resolve any major crises and by 1938 it was no longer a major player. The League was undermined by the bellicosity of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Japan" title="Imperial Japan">Imperial Japan</a>, the Soviet Union, and <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Mussolini's</a> Italy, and by the non-participation of the United States.</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_at_Great_Wall,_Laiyuan,_Hebei,_autumn_1937.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="910" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Battle_at_Great_Wall%2C_Laiyuan%2C_Hebei%2C_autumn_1937.jpg/220px-Battle_at_Great_Wall%2C_Laiyuan%2C_Hebei%2C_autumn_1937.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Battle_at_Great_Wall%2C_Laiyuan%2C_Hebei%2C_autumn_1937.jpg/330px-Battle_at_Great_Wall%2C_Laiyuan%2C_Hebei%2C_autumn_1937.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Battle_at_Great_Wall%2C_Laiyuan%2C_Hebei%2C_autumn_1937.jpg/440px-Battle_at_Great_Wall%2C_Laiyuan%2C_Hebei%2C_autumn_1937.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_at_Great_Wall,_Laiyuan,_Hebei,_autumn_1937.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Nationalist Chinese</a> soldiers defending at the Battle at Great Wall, Laiyuan, <a href="/wiki/Hebei" title="Hebei">Hebei</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> autumn 1937. The <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese war</a> cost at least twenty millions lives.</div></div></div><p>A series of international crises strained the League to its limits, the earliest being the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">invasion of Manchuria</a> by Japan and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abyssinian_crisis" title="Abyssinian crisis">Abyssinian crisis</a> of 1935/36 in which Italy invaded <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire" title="Ethiopian Empire">Abyssinia</a>, one of the only free African nations at that time.
</p><p>The League tried to enforce economic sanctions upon Italy, but to no avail. The incident highlighted French and British weakness, exemplified by their reluctance to alienate Italy and lose her as their ally. The limited actions taken by the Western powers pushed Mussolini's Italy towards alliance with Hitler's Germany anyway. The Abyssinian war showed Hitler how weak the League was and encouraged the remilitarization of the Rhineland in flagrant disregard of the Treaty of Versailles. This was the first in a series of provocative acts culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">invasion of Poland</a> in September 1939 and the beginning of the Second World War.
</p>
<h3><span id="Tripartite_Pact.2C_World_War_II_and_contemporary_history_.28post-1945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tripartite_Pact,_World_War_II_and_contemporary_history_(post-1945)">Tripartite Pact, World War II and contemporary history (post-1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Tripartite Pact, World War II and contemporary history (post-1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hungry for raw materials and pressed by a growing population, Japan initiated the seizure of <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a> in September 1931 and established ex-Qing emperor <a href="/wiki/Puyi" title="Puyi">Puyi</a> as head of the <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">puppet state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Manchukuo" title="Manchukuo">Manchukuo</a> in 1932. During the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Sino-Japanese War (1937–1945)</a>, the loss of Manchuria, and its vast potential for industrial development and war industries, was a blow to the Kuomintang economy. After 1940, conflicts between the Kuomintang and Communists became more frequent in the <a href="/wiki/Free_China_(Second_Sino-Japanese_War)" title="Free China (Second Sino-Japanese War)">areas not under Japanese control</a>. The Communists expanded their influence wherever opportunities presented themselves through mass organizations, administrative reforms, and the land- and tax-reform measures favoring the peasants—while the Kuomintang attempted to neutralize the spread of Communist influence.The <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> had seen tensions rise between Imperial Japan and the United States; events such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panay_incident" title="Panay incident">Panay incident</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanking_Massacre" title="Nanking Massacre">Nanking Massacre</a> turned American public opinion against Japan. With the occupation of <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">French Indochina</a> in the years of 1940–41, and with the continuing war in China, the United States placed embargoes on Japan of <a href="/wiki/Strategic_material" title="Strategic material">strategic materials</a> such as scrap metal and oil, which were vitally needed for the war effort. The Japanese were faced with the option of either withdrawing from China and losing face or seizing and securing new sources of raw materials in the resource-rich, European-controlled colonies of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>—specifically <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">British Malaya</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>). In 1940, Imperial Japan signed the <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">Tripartite Pact</a> with Nazi Germany and Fascist Italy.
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a></div>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ww2_allied_axis_1942_jun.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1480" decoding="async" height="297" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ww2_allied_axis_1942_jun.png/700px-Ww2_allied_axis_1942_jun.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ww2_allied_axis_1942_jun.png/1050px-Ww2_allied_axis_1942_jun.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ww2_allied_axis_1942_jun.png/1400px-Ww2_allied_axis_1942_jun.png 2x" width="700"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ww2_allied_axis_1942_jun.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>World War II at the height of Axis expansion (black) fighting against the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> (blue) and <a href="/wiki/Communist_International" title="Communist International">Comintern</a> (red). It is important to note that the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> was not at war with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> despite being part of the <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">Tripartite Pact</a>.</div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-012-0037-23A,_Polen,_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf,_Infanterie.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-012-0037-23A%2C_Polen%2C_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf%2C_Infanterie.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-012-0037-23A%2C_Polen%2C_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf%2C_Infanterie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-012-0037-23A%2C_Polen%2C_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf%2C_Infanterie.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-012-0037-23A%2C_Polen%2C_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf%2C_Infanterie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-012-0037-23A%2C_Polen%2C_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf%2C_Infanterie.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-012-0037-23A%2C_Polen%2C_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf%2C_Infanterie.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-012-0037-23A,_Polen,_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf,_Infanterie.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The German <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">Invasion of Poland</a> in 1939 is the official start of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">WWII</a></div></div></div>
<p>Even though Japan had been invading in China since 1937, the conventional view is that the World War II began on September 1, 1939, when <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> invaded Poland, the <a href="/wiki/Drang_nach_Osten" title="Drang nach Osten">Drang nach Osten</a>. Within two days the United Kingdom and France declared war on Germany, even though the fighting was confined to Poland. Pursuant to a then-secret provision of its non-aggression <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact</a>, the Soviet Union joined with Germany on September 17, 1939, to conquer Poland and to divide Eastern Europe.
The <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> were initially made up of Poland, the United Kingdom, France, Australia, Canada, New Zealand, South Africa, as well as <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">British Commonwealth</a> countries which were controlled directly by the UK, such as the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">Indian Empire</a>. All of these countries declared war on Germany in September 1939.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Children_in_the_Holocaust_concentration_camp_liberated_by_Red_Army.jpg"><img alt="Holocaust Survivors, January 1945" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="578" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Children_in_the_Holocaust_concentration_camp_liberated_by_Red_Army.jpg/220px-Children_in_the_Holocaust_concentration_camp_liberated_by_Red_Army.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Children_in_the_Holocaust_concentration_camp_liberated_by_Red_Army.jpg/330px-Children_in_the_Holocaust_concentration_camp_liberated_by_Red_Army.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Children_in_the_Holocaust_concentration_camp_liberated_by_Red_Army.jpg/440px-Children_in_the_Holocaust_concentration_camp_liberated_by_Red_Army.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Children_in_the_Holocaust_concentration_camp_liberated_by_Red_Army.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Survivors of the <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">Holocaust</a> at the infamous German concentration camp of <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz</a> located in Occupied Poland.</div></div></div>
<p>Following the lull in fighting, known as the "<a href="/wiki/Phoney_War" title="Phoney War">Phoney War</a>", Germany invaded western Europe in May 1940. Six weeks later, France, in the meantime, attacked by Italy as well, surrendered to Germany, which then tried unsuccessfully to conquer Britain. On September 27, Germany, Italy, and Japan signed a mutual defense agreement, the <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">Tripartite Pact</a>, and were known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a>. Nine months later, on June 22, 1941, Germany launched a massive invasion of the Soviet Union, which promptly joined the Allies. Germany was now engaged in fighting a war on two fronts. This proved to be a mistake by Germany – Germany had not successfully carried out the invasion of Britain and the war turned against the Axis.
</p><p>On December 7, 1941, <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">Japan attacked the United States at Pearl Harbor</a>, bringing it too into the war on the Allied side. China also joined the Allies, as eventually did most of the rest of the world. China was in turmoil at the time, and attacked Japanese armies through guerilla-type warfare. By the beginning of 1942, the major combatants were aligned as follows: the British Commonwealth, the United States, and the Soviet Union were fighting Germany and Italy; and the British Commonwealth, China, and the United States were fighting Japan. The United Kingdom, the United States, the Soviet Union and China were referred as a "trusteeship of the powerful" during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Justus_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Justus-77">[76]</a></sup> and were recognized as the Allied "Big Four" in <a href="/wiki/Declaration_by_United_Nations" title="Declaration by United Nations">Declaration by United Nations</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> These four countries were considered as the "<a href="/wiki/Four_Policemen" title="Four Policemen">Four Policemen</a>" or "Four Sheriffs" of the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies power</a> and primary victors of World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> From then through August 1945, battles raged across all of Europe, in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Ocean" title="North Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic Ocean</a>, across North Africa, throughout <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, throughout China, across the Pacific Ocean and in the air over Japan.
Italy surrendered in September 1943 and was split into a northern Germany-occupied <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">puppet state</a> and an Allies-friendly state in the South; Germany surrendered in May 1945. Following the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">Japan surrendered</a>, marking the end of the war on September 2, 1945.
</p>
