Truman">Harry Truman's</a> speech regarding the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">nuclear attack</a> on <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima" title="Hiroshima">Hiroshima, Japan</a>. Captions provided</div></div></div>
<p>It is possible that around 62 million people <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties" title="World War II casualties">died in the war</a>; estimates vary greatly. About 60% of all casualties were civilians, who died as a result of disease, starvation, <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> (in particular, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocaust" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a>), and aerial bombing. The former Soviet Union and China suffered the most casualties. Estimates place deaths in the Soviet Union at around 23 million, while China suffered about 10 million. No country lost a greater portion of its population than Poland: approximately 5.6 million, or 16%, of its pre-war population of 34.8 million died.
The Holocaust (which roughly means "burnt whole") was the deliberate and systematic murder of millions of Jews and other "unwanted" during World War II by the Nazi regime in Germany. Several differing views exist regarding whether it was intended to occur from the war's beginning, or if the plans for it came about later. Regardless, persecution of Jews extended well before the war even started, such as in the <i><a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a></i> (Night of Broken Glass). The Nazis used propaganda to great effect to stir up anti-Semitic feelings within ordinary Germans.
</p><p>After World War II, Europe was informally split into Western and Soviet <a href="/wiki/Sphere_of_influence" title="Sphere of influence">spheres of influence</a>. <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> later aligned as the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organization</a> (NATO) and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>. There was a shift in power from Western Europe and the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> to the two new superpowers, the United States and the Soviet Union. These two rivals would later face off in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. In Asia, the defeat of Japan led to its <a href="/wiki/Democratization" title="Democratization">democratization</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">China's civil war</a> continued through and after the war, resulting eventually in the establishment of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>. The former colonies of the European powers began their road to independence.
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_history" title="Contemporary history">Contemporary history</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_i_H%C3%B6torgscity_1963.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1607" data-file-width="1446" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/The_Beatles_i_H%C3%B6torgscity_1963.jpg/180px-The_Beatles_i_H%C3%B6torgscity_1963.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/The_Beatles_i_H%C3%B6torgscity_1963.jpg/270px-The_Beatles_i_H%C3%B6torgscity_1963.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/The_Beatles_i_H%C3%B6torgscity_1963.jpg/360px-The_Beatles_i_H%C3%B6torgscity_1963.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_i_H%C3%B6torgscity_1963.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>During <a href="/wiki/Pax_Americana" title="Pax Americana">Pax Americana</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">popular music industry</a> flourished. Pictured here is the <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">Beatles</a> Group.</div></div></div>
<p>The mid-20th century is distinguished from most of human history in that its most significant changes were directly or indirectly economic and technological in nature. Economic development was the force behind vast changes in everyday life, to a degree which was unprecedented in human history.
</p><p>Over the course of the 20th century, the world's per-capita <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> grew by a factor of five,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> much more than all earlier centuries combined (including the 19th with its Industrial Revolution). Many economists make the case that this understates the magnitude of growth, as many of the goods and services consumed at the end of the 20th century, such as improved medicine (causing world life expectancy to increase by more than two decades) and communications technologies, were not available at any price at its beginning.  However, the gulf between the world's rich and poor grew wider,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> and the majority of the global population remained in the poor side of the divide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>Still, advancing technology and medicine has had a great impact even in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">Global South</a>. Large-scale industry and more centralized <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">media</a> made brutal dictatorships possible on an unprecedented scale in the middle of the century, leading to wars that were also unprecedented. However, the increased communications contributed to <a href="/wiki/Democratization" title="Democratization">democratization</a>. Technological developments included the development of airplanes and <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space exploration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_technology" title="Nuclear technology">nuclear technology</a>, advancement in <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a>, and the dawning of the <a href="/wiki/Information_Age" title="Information Age">Information Age</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pax_Americana">Pax Americana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Pax Americana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pax_Americana" title="Pax Americana">Pax Americana</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/American_Century" title="American Century">American Century</a></div>
<p>Pax Americana is an appellation applied to the historical concept of relative liberal peace in the Western world, resulting from the preponderance of power enjoyed by the United States of America starting around the start of the 20th century. Although the term finds its primary utility in the latter half of the 20th century, it has been used in various places and eras. Its modern connotations concern the peace established after the end of World War II in 1945.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War_era">Cold War era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Cold War era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a></div>
<p>The Cold War began in the mid-1940s and lasted into the early 1990s. Throughout this period, the conflict was expressed through military coalitions, espionage, weapons development, invasions, propaganda, and competitive technological development. The conflict included costly defense spending, a massive <a href="/wiki/Conventional_weapon" title="Conventional weapon">conventional</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear</a> <a href="/wiki/Arms_race" title="Arms race">arms race</a>, and numerous <a href="/wiki/Proxy_war" title="Proxy war">proxy wars</a>; the two <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpowers</a> never fought one another directly.
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NATO_vs._Warsaw_(1949-1990).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/NATO_vs._Warsaw_%281949-1990%29.svg/750px-NATO_vs._Warsaw_%281949-1990%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/NATO_vs._Warsaw_%281949-1990%29.svg/1125px-NATO_vs._Warsaw_%281949-1990%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/NATO_vs._Warsaw_%281949-1990%29.svg/1500px-NATO_vs._Warsaw_%281949-1990%29.svg.png 2x" width="750"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NATO_vs._Warsaw_(1949-1990).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Borders of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> (blue) and <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> (red) states during the Cold war era.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The Soviet Union created the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> of countries that it occupied, annexing some as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Socialist_Republics" title="Soviet Socialist Republics">Soviet Socialist Republics</a> and maintaining others as satellite states that would later form the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>. The United States and various western European countries began a policy of "<a href="/wiki/Containment" title="Containment">containment</a>" of <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communism</a> and forged myriad alliances to this end, including <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. Several of these western countries also coordinated efforts regarding the rebuilding of western Europe, including western Germany, which the Soviets opposed. In other regions of the world, such as Latin America and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, the Soviet Union fostered <a href="/wiki/Communist_revolution" title="Communist revolution">communist revolutionary</a> movements, which the United States and many of its allies opposed and, in some cases, attempted to "<a href="/wiki/Rollback" title="Rollback">roll back</a>". Many countries were prompted to align themselves with the nations that would later form either NATO or the Warsaw Pact, the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> emerged from nations who desired neutrality.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="405" data-file-width="555" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg/220px-US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg/330px-US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg/440px-US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>US and USSR nuclear stockpiles</div></div></div>
<p>In China <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> (<i>Máo zé dōng</i>) utilized <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxism-Leninism" title="Marxism-Leninism">Marxist–Leninist</a> thought. When the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party of China</a> assumed power in 1949, previous schools of Chinese thought, excepting notably <a href="/wiki/Legalism_(Chinese_philosophy)" title="Legalism (Chinese philosophy)">Legalism</a>, were denounced as backward. Many parts of China's past were even purged during the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a>. Though initially friendly with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> the Chinese and Soviet communists diverged in the <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">Sino-Soviet split</a> of 1960. Through the end of the Cold-War, China would continue on its own path from other communist countries, building better relations with the United States after 1972. China's economy would recover from the Cultural Revolution due to <a href="/wiki/Chinese_economic_reform" title="Chinese economic reform">market-oriented reforms</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping" title="Deng Xiaoping">Deng Xiaoping</a>.
</p><p>The Cold War saw periods of both heightened tension and relative calm. International crises arose, such as the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Blockade" title="Berlin Blockade">Berlin Blockade</a> (1948–1949), the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> (1950–1953), the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Crisis_of_1961" title="Berlin Crisis of 1961">Berlin Crisis of 1961</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> (1955–1975), the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a> (1962), the <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War" title="Soviet–Afghan War">Soviet–Afghan War</a> (1979–1989) and <a href="/wiki/Able_Archer_83" title="Able Archer 83">NATO exercises in November 1983</a>. There were also periods of reduced tension as both sides sought <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9tente" title="Détente">détente</a>. Direct military attacks on adversaries were deterred by the potential for <a href="/wiki/Mutual_assured_destruction" title="Mutual assured destruction">mutual assured destruction</a> using deliverable <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a>.
</p>
<table style="margin:auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:264px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europe_1988.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="262" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/63/Europe_1988.png" width="262"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europe_1988.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>European <a href="/wiki/Trade_bloc" title="Trade bloc">trade blocs</a> as of the late 1980s. EEC member states are marked in blue, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EFTA" title="EFTA">EFTA</a> – green, and Comecon – red.</div></div></div>
</td>
<td><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cold_War_Map_1980.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="477" data-file-width="940" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cold_War_Map_1980.svg/330px-Cold_War_Map_1980.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cold_War_Map_1980.svg/495px-Cold_War_Map_1980.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cold_War_Map_1980.svg/660px-Cold_War_Map_1980.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cold_War_Map_1980.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>East and West in 1980, as defined by the Cold War. The Cold War had divided Europe politically into East and West, with the Iron Curtain splitting <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>.</div></div></div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The Cold War drew to a close in the late 1980s and the early 1990s. The United States under President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> increased diplomatic, military, and economic pressure on the Soviet Union, which was already suffering from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brezhnev_stagnation" title="Brezhnev stagnation">severe economic stagnation</a>. In the second half of the 1980s, newly appointed Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a> introduced the <i><a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">perestroika</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">glasnost</a></i> reforms. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1985%E2%80%931991)" title="History of the Soviet Union (1985–1991)">The Soviet Union collapsed</a> in 1991, leaving the United States as the dominant military power, though Russia retained much of the massive Soviet nuclear arsenal.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America_polarization">Latin America polarization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Latin America polarization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Latin America in the 1970s, leftists acquired a significant political influence which prompted the right-wing, ecclesiastical authorities and a large portion of the individual country's upper class to support coups d'état to avoid what they perceived as a communist threat. This was further fueled by Cuban and United States intervention which led to a political polarization. Most South American countries were in some periods ruled by <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">military dictatorships</a> that were supported by the United States of America. In the 1970s, the regimes of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">Southern Cone</a> collaborated in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">Operation Condor</a> killing many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leftist" title="Leftist">leftist</a> dissidents, including some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_guerrilla" title="Urban guerrilla">urban guerrillas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> However, by the early 1990s all countries had restored their democracies.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Space_Age">Space Age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Space Age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Space_Age" title="Space Age">Space Age</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><audio class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="25" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Neil_Armstrong_small_step.wav" id="mwe_player_8" preload="none" style="width:220px;" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="52184" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg Vorbis" data-title="Ogg Vorbis" data-transcodekey="ogg" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/bb/Neil_Armstrong_small_step.wav/Neil_Armstrong_small_step.wav.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="88200" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="WAV source" data-title="Original WAV file (88 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bb/Neil_Armstrong_small_step.wav" type="audio/wav"/><source data-bandwidth="103584" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/bb/Neil_Armstrong_small_step.wav/Neil_Armstrong_small_step.wav.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/><track data-dir="ltr" kind="subtitles" label="English ‪(en)‬" src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3ANeil_Armstrong_small_step.wav&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt&amp;origin=%2A" srclang="en" type="text/vtt"/></audio> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Neil_Armstrong_small_step.wav" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">Neil Armstrong</a>'s small step on the Moon during <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">Apollo 11</a>, July 20, 1969</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3002" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/220px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/330px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/440px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/The_Blue_Marble" title="The Blue Marble">The Blue Marble</a></i>, a 1972 photograph of Earth as seen from <a href="/wiki/Apollo_17" title="Apollo 17">Apollo 17</a>. The second half of the 20th century saw an increase of interest in both <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space exploration</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_movement" title="Environmental movement">environmental movement</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The Space Age is a period encompassing the activities related to the <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a>, <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space exploration</a>, space technology, and the cultural developments influenced by these events. The Space Age began with the development of several technologies that culminated with the launch of <a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">Sputnik 1</a> by the Soviet Union in October 1957. This was the world's first artificial satellite, orbiting the Earth in 98.1 minutes and weighing in at 83 kg. The launch of Sputnik 1 ushered a new era of political, scientific and technological achievements that became known as the Space Age. The Space Age was characterized by rapid development of new technology in a close race mostly between the United States and the Soviet Union. The Space Age brought the first human spaceflight during the <a href="/wiki/Vostok_programme" title="Vostok programme">Vostok programme</a> and reached its peak with the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo program</a> which captured the imagination of much of the world's population. The 1969 landing of <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">Apollo 11</a> on the Moon was an event watched by over 500 million people around the world and is widely recognized as one of the defining moments of the 20th century. Since then, and with the end of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_race" title="Space race">space race</a> due to the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, public attention has largely moved to other areas.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Information_Age">Information Age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_modern_period&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Information Age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Information_Age" title="Information Age">Information Age</a></div>
<p>The Information Age began in the mid-20th century, characterized by a rapid <a href="/wiki/Epoch" title="Epoch">epochal</a> shift from the traditional industry established by the Industrial Revolution to an economy primarily based upon <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Idea_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Idea-85">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manuel_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Manuel-5">[5]</a></sup> The onset of the Information Age can be associated with the development of <a href="/wiki/Transistor" title="Transistor">transistor</a> technology,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manuel_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-Manuel-5">[5]</a></sup> particularly the <a href="/wiki/MOSFET" title="MOSFET">MOSFET</a> (metal-oxide-<a href="/wiki/Semiconductor" title="Semiconductor">semiconductor</a> <a href="/wiki/Field-effect_transistor" title="Field-effect transistor">field-effect transistor</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raymer_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Raymer-87">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-triumph_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-triumph-88">[87]</a></sup> which became the fundamental building block of <a href="/wiki/Digital_electronics" title="Digital electronics">digital electronics</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raymer_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-Raymer-87">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-triumph_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-triumph-88">[87]</a></sup> and revolutionized <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_technology" title="Modern technology">modern technology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manuel_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-Manuel-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cressler_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cressler-89">[88]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Public_Administration_Network" title="United Nations Public Administration Network">United Nations Public Administration Network</a>, the Information Age was formed by <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">capitalizing</a> on <a href="/wiki/Miniaturization" title="Miniaturization">computer microminiaturization</a> advances,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> which, upon broader usage within society, would lead to <a href="/wiki/Modernization_theory" title="Modernization theory">modernized</a> <a href="/wiki/Information" title="Information">information</a> and to communication processes becoming the driving force of <a href="/wiki/Sociocultural_evolution" title="Sociocultural evolution">social evolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Idea_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-Idea-85">[84]</a></sup>
</p>

Oxford University Press. 2007. <q>humanism <i>n.</i> 1 a rationalistic system of thought attaching prime importance to human rather than divine or supernatural matters. 2 a Renaissance cultural movement that turned away from medieval scholastic-ism and revived interest in ancient Greek and Roman thought.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Compact+Oxford+English+Dictionary&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALate+modern+period"></span> Typically, abridgments of this definition omit all senses except #1, such as in the <a class="external text" href="http://dictionary.cambridge.org/define.asp?key=38402&amp;dict=CALD" rel="nofollow"><i>Cambridge Advanced Learner's Dictionary</i></a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20031230202029/http://dictionary.cambridge.org/define.asp?key=38402&amp;dict=CALD" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 2003-12-30 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.thefreedictionary.com/humanism" rel="nofollow"><i>Collins Essential English Dictionary</i></a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110606152758/http://www.thefreedictionary.com/humanism" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 2011-06-06 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>, and <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1"><span class="cs1-lock-registration" title="Free registration required"><a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/webstersconcised00rand" rel="nofollow"><i>Webster's Concise Dictionary</i></a></span>. <li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1"><i>Collins Concise Dictionary</i>. HarperCollins (published 1990). 1999. <q>The rejection of religion in favour of a belief in the advancement of humanity by its own efforts.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Collins+Concise+Dictionary&amp;rft.pub=HarperCollins&amp;rft.date=1999&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALate+modern+period"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the 1888 English edition of the <i>Communist Manifest</i>, <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Engels" title="Friedrich Engels">Friedrich Engels</a> added a footnote with the commentary: "That is, all written history. In 1847, the prehistory of society, the social organization existing previous to recorded history, was all but unknown. Since then Haxthausen discovered common ownership of land In Russia, Maurer concluded it to be the social foundation from which all Teutonic races started in history, and by and by village communities were found to be, or to have been, the primitive form of society everywhere from India to Ireland. The Inner organization of this primitive Communistic society was laid bare, In its typical form, by Morgan's work on the true nature of the gens and Its relation to the tribe. With the dissolution of these primaeval communities society begins to be differentiated into separate and finally antagonistic classes. I have attempte to retrace this process of dissolution in "<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Der_Ursprung_der_Familie,_des_Privateigenthums_und_des_Staats" title="Der Ursprung der Familie, des Privateigenthums und des Staats">Der Ursprung der Familie, des Privateigenthums und des Staats</a></i>"", from Marx, Karl, Friedrich Engels, Leon Trotsky, and Karl Marx. <i><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=dEyEzazZKwIC&amp;pg=PA46" rel="nofollow">The Communist Manifesto and Its Relevance for Today</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160427014730/https://books.google.com/books?id=dEyEzazZKwIC&amp;pg=PA46" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 2016-04-27 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a></i>. Chippendale, N.S.W.: Resistance Books, 1998. p. 46, see also <i><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=p7s0oTEWB_MC&amp;pg=PA204" rel="nofollow">Cornelius Castoriadis, Political and Social Writings</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160624164213/https://books.google.com/books?id=p7s0oTEWB_MC&amp;pg=PA204" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 2016-06-24 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a></i>. Minneapolis: University of Minnesota Press, 1993. p. 204</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-53">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Marx makes no claim to have produced a master key to history. Historical materialism is not "an historico-philosophic theory of the marche generale imposed by fate upon every people, whatever the historic circumstances in which it finds itself". (Marx, Karl, Letter to editor of the Russian paper <i>Otetchestvennye Zapiskym</i>, 1877) His ideas, he explains, are based on a concrete study of the actual conditions that pertained in Europe.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Most notably by dividing the British crown into several sovereignties by the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Patriation" title="Patriation">patriation</a> of constitutions by the <a href="/wiki/Canada_Act_1982" title="Canada Act 1982">Canada Act 1982</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Australia_Act_1986" title="Australia Act 1986">Australia Act 1986</a>, and by the independence of countries such as India, Pakistan, South Africa, and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>.</span>

<li id="cite_note-Cressler-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Cressler_89-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFCresslerMantooth2017">Cressler, John D.; Mantooth, H. Alan (2017). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=4AlEDwAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA959" rel="nofollow"><i>Extreme Environment Electronics</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/CRC_Press" title="CRC Press">CRC Press</a>. p. 959. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-351-83280-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-351-83280-9"><bdi>978-1-351-83280-9</bdi></a>. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20200803075936/https://books.google.com/books?id=4AlEDwAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA959" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> from the original on 2020-08-03<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2021-04-01</span></span>. <q>While the bipolar junction transistor was the first transistor device to take hold in the integrated circuit world, there is no question that the advent of MOSFETs, an acronym for metal-oxide-semiconductor field-effect transistor, is what truly revolutionized the world in the so-called information age. The density with which these devices can be made has allowed entire computers to exist on a few small chips rather than filling a room.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Extreme+Environment+Electronics&amp;rft.pages=959&amp;rft.pub=CRC+Press&amp;rft.date=2017&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-351-83280-9&amp;rft.aulast=Cressler&amp;rft.aufirst=John+D.&amp;rft.au=Mantooth%2C+H.+Alan&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D4AlEDwAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA959&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALate+modern+period"></span></span>

<ul><li>1: <b>Creation</b> - <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">Big Bang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cosmogony" title="Cosmogony">cosmogony</a></li>
